Central Propaganda Department Receives the Press 63

The Central Propaganda Department held a press conference at 2:00 PM on the 12th in the Second Conference Hall of the Central Party Headquarters. More than twenty reporters from various newspapers attended. Zhang Tingxiu chaired the meeting and introduced Central Committee Member Miao Peicheng, who reported on the situation of Party affairs in the North and the general public's understanding of the current war. Miao's report mainly stated that since March 20th, Party headquarters in Beiping, Tianjin, Chahar, Suiyuan, Hebei, and Shanxi had been destroyed by reactionary forces. Although they were superficially affected, actual work continued. Since the Party headquarters in the North were occupied by reactionary forces, different factions had been disputing and attacking each other for months without any results, and the situation had reached a stalemate. Reactionaries in the North still hoped that Wang Jingwei would come north, but based on general observation, even if Wang went north, there would be no way to resolve the disturbances. The people in the North believed that Yan and Feng's reckless actions this time were meaningless and only disrupted social order. Therefore, they resisted Yan and Feng's tax increases. Even the lower-level officers and soldiers under Yan and Feng felt that this war was absurd. Even the propaganda personnel did not understand the reasons for this war. Therefore, based on these observations, the North has a widespread understanding of right and wrong. Feng and Yan's regressive actions were even worse than those of the warlords, so their failure was very rapid. The meeting adjourned after the report.

Battles Occur Near Fuzhou 64

At the same time, a fire broke out in the city. A Fuzhou correspondent reports that Liu He and Ding Luxingbang's divisions have reinforced their defenses outside the northwest of the provincial capital since the 7th, contact has been made. The situation at the front and rear is described separately below. On the morning of the 5th, Liu's division learned that Lu's division had sent Chen Rongbiao's regiment to station at Xiaobeiling in the northwest center (30 li from the provincial capital), approaching the defense area of Jiang Yan's regiment of the division's Lingtou Township. A military conference was immediately convened, and it was resolved to send a telegram to Lu Xingbang requesting him to quickly withdraw the regiment to its original defense to avoid misunderstandings. By the morning of the 7th, no reply had been received. Chen's regiment continued to advance, and the two sides' outposts began contact at 11:00 AM. By 10:00 PM, the fighting gradually intensified, and the battle line gradually expanded. The northern route extended from the right side of Xiaobeiling to Ma'anshan, 10 li from the North Gate, and the western route extended from the left side of Xiaobeiling to Jinjishan, 10 li from the West Gate. Both sides occupied the mountain peaks and fired at each other with machine guns and mortars. The sound of gunfire was extremely dense in the city. At 8:00 AM on the 8th, Liu's division used heavy artillery to attack Lu's division. Lu's division retreated to Beiling on the northern route (40 li from the provincial capital). Liu's division occupied Ma'an and Jinji mountains, and the Huangdian arsenal was also recovered. The fighting subsided slightly. At 10:00 PM on the 8th, Lu's division sent reinforcements of about one regiment to attack Ma'an, returning from Beiling over Lingtou at night. Liu's division also returned fire with artillery. The sound of cannons continued all night. Looking into the distance from high ground, smoke and fire could be seen rising from the mountain peaks. At 8:00 AM on the 9th, Liu's division used a charge formation to force Lu's troops back to the Meiting and Baofu mountains on the western route (about 15 li from the provincial capital). The two armies were still fiercely fighting on the Western front but the sound of artillery fire was no longer heard in the city. The combat troops on both sides were Chen Rongbiao's regiment on the northern route and Qian Yuguang's regiment on the western route. The reserve team was Wang Tianrui's regiment, totaling about 6,000 people. The commander was Yu Bailiang, chief of staff of the division headquarters. The command post was located in Xiangzhe in the western countryside. Liu's division's Northern front regiment was Jiang Yan's regiment, the western regiment was Yan Ximin's regiment. The reserve team was Tang Lin's regiment, also with 6,000 soldiers. The commander was Brigade Commander Liu Shangzhi, and the command post was located in West Lake Park. On the 8th, Liu's division also transferred Chen Wantai's entire brigade from Quanzhou to the provincial capital, which will rotate with Liu Shangzhi and Gui Zhenyuan's brigades to the front line for combat. Furthermore, the division announced that as a result of the three days of combat on the 7th, 8th, and 9th, Lu's troops suffered more than 200 casualties and more than 500 were captured. One battalion commander was captured, and more than 20 machine guns and mortars and more than 400 rifles were seized. After the fighting broke out in Fuzhou City on the 7th, the initial situation was quite stable. Later, due to nightfall, a group of hooligans specialized in setting fires everywhere in an attempt to disrupt the rear. At about 7:00 PM, Dongmen Street and Qixunkou near the 56th Division Headquarters successively caught fire, each burning down more than ten houses. Fortunately, residents in other places discovered and immediately extinguished the fires. At the same time, all the city's electric lights went out, and the situation suddenly became tense. Shops closed one after another, and pedestrians were extremely scarce. Military and police agencies immediately dispatched teams to patrol, and fire brigades from various shops also summoned rescue workers, divided up fire-fighting equipment, and conducted patrols. On the 8th, it was discovered that some unscrupulous elements were carrying short guns and hand grenades, taking the opportunity to make trouble. Each street and alley has now set up barricades and organized joint defenses for self-protection. The Provincial Defense Command also issued a notice stating that any patrol officers or police who captured these troublemakers would be executed on the spot to serve as a warning. However, shops have been closed since the 7th, and the exchange rate for small silver coins has risen from 72 to 80 wen per coin. The price of white rice has risen from 12 yuan to 16 yuan per shi. Many wealthy families in the city have moved to the South Bank naval defense area in Taiwan to live. (June 9th)

Japanese Navy Causes Trouble Again in Hankou 65

Runs over and kills Sergeant Yang Ruiwen of the Traveling Headquarters. Hankou Correspondence: At 3:00 PM on the 10th, at the intersection of Paris Street and Dituomei Consulate Street in the French Concession, a Japanese Navy cargo truck without license plates, driven recklessly by Japanese sailor Nakaoshigei Masaaki, ran over Yang Ruiwen, a sergeant and orderly in the office of the Chief of Staff of the Commander-in-Chief's Traveling Headquarters, killing him instantly with a fractured skull and brains splattered out. The situation was extremely tragic. The Traveling Headquarters sent Secretary Wu Qi to negotiate with the Hankou Local Court, which dispatched Prosecutor Liao Yuan to the scene for inspection. The details of this case are described as follows: Incident Circumstances: At 2:20 PM, Sergeant Yang Ruiwen, an orderly in the office of the Chief of Staff of the Traveling Headquarters, was riding his bicycle on official business to the French Concession. He was traveling north on Paris Street and wanted to turn onto Simin Street. As he was about to turn, a Japanese Navy cargo truck without license plates was speeding east on Simin Street, wanting to turn onto Paris Street. Yang was unable to avoid it and was knocked down by the truck at the intersection of Paris Street and Dituomei Consulate Street, shattering his skull and brains. He died instantly. The French military police on duty at the scene only took the driver, Japanese Nakaoshigei Masaaki, to the French police station, while the truck was allowed to escape. Culprit's Confession: After being taken to the police station by the French patrol police, the Japanese sailor Nakaoshigei Masaaki was interrogated by the French police authorities at 3:20 PM. According to his confession, an Annamese patrol police officer in the street at the time had directed him to stop, but it was too late to prevent running over Yang Ruiwen. Yang Ruiwen, the deceased, was 19 years old and from Bengbu. The bicycle number was 923, which has also been verified. Note on Inspection: After receiving the report, Wang Jue, Chief Prosecutor of the Local Court, dispatched the duty prosecutor Liao Yuan, clerk Yan Xun, inspector Cheng Zhidao, and four French police officers to the scene for inspection. Inspector Cheng examined the body and found a total of four injuries: (1) The skull was broken into five pieces, and the brains were completely splattered out. (2) Scratches on the right shoulder. (3) Scratches on the right arm.

Page 9

Essential News from the Republic of China, 19th Year

(4) Blood in the mouth and nose. The head injury was confirmed to be fatal. After the inspection, a letter was sent to the French police station requesting the extradition of the culprit to be tried according to the law. The victim's body was prepared with a coffin by the adjutant's office of the Traveling Headquarters for burial. Negotiation Process: After receiving the report, the Chief of Staff's Traveling Headquarters sent a letter to the French police station requesting that the culprit, the Japanese, be handed over to our country's court for handling. At the same time, Secretary Wu Qi and Adjutant Lai Shousong were sent to negotiate. French Consul Bostede refused to hand over the culprit, claiming that he had no authority to handle Japanese Navy personnel. After repeated negotiations by Wu and others, they argued that the Chinese government should send a letter to the Japanese Consul requesting extradition, and the French police station should not release the culprit freely. Finally, Japanese Consul Kokone came to the French police station and negotiated three times. As a result, the culprit confessed that he was a current Japanese naval seaman named Nakaoshigei Masaaki. The Japanese Consul temporarily took him away, promising to hand him over at any time if the Chinese court requested an interrogation. The French Consul also took responsibility for handing over the culprit at any time for court summons. (June 11th)

The Beginning and End of the Shantou Strike 66

Report from the Provincial Government Inspector on the Mediation Process. Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, Shantou merchants went on strike to protest the surcharge on electricity bills for military expenses. The truth of the matter was largely unknown outside. At the time, political circles accused the merchants of disrupting finances by resisting taxes, while the merchants believed that the surcharge on electricity bills was a temporary miscellaneous tax that merchants and residents could not bear for long. Moreover, the surcharge had already been submitted to the government for cancellation, but the municipal authorities were still collecting it as before, which seemed to disregard the law. The two sides went to extremes, and on the 21st of last month, police officers clashed with the accountant of the Jiacheng Silver Store when collecting the surcharge. The accountant was detained in the police station, and all the merchants and residents of the city unanimously went on strike in protest. The situation has been briefly described in previous reports. Later, Huang Zungeng, the inspector sent by the provincial government to the Chao-Shan area, mediated between the two parties. As a result, the municipal government canceled the surcharge, and if municipal expenses were insufficient, methods would be found to raise funds from the local area. The strike ended. In order to make the truth clear to readers, we have sought and recorded Huang Zungeng's report to the provincial government on the beginning and end of the case as follows: (It has been found that the surcharge on electricity in Shantou was levied in the 15th year of the Republic of China when the revolutionary army swore to launch the Northern Expedition. Due to the lack of military funds, a 10% surcharge was levied on all electricity in the city, which was intended to be used as temporary military expenses for the Northern Expedition. Later, Mayor Xiao Guanying submitted a request to the Guangdong Finance Department, which approved the allocation of the funds to municipal expenses. The burden on the citizens was endless. Various commercial groups petitioned the city's General Chamber of Commerce and the Commercial and Civil Coordination Association to submit a request to the government for cancellation. The government approved the cancellation in consideration of the merchants' difficulties. When Mayor Xu Xiqing stated that the electricity surcharge funds had already been included in the annual budget by previous mayors and that cancellation would be difficult, he requested approval to withdraw the cancellation order and maintain the original plan for continued collection in order to support municipal administration. The government approved the request for continued implementation. Recently, the National Government issued an order that all surcharges levied for military purposes should be canceled. The merchants and residents believed that the electricity surcharge in Shantou was a type of temporary military expense for the Northern Expedition and should be included in the list of cancellations. They repeatedly requested the municipal government to cancel it, but the municipal government refused, citing the city treasury's deficit. The surcharge was originally collected by the Electricity Bureau. Later, the merchants and residents negotiated with the Electricity Bureau to reduce the price and established an Electricity Price Reduction Committee to deal with the situation. Later, the municipal government saw this situation and took back the self-management. The merchants and residents believed that electricity was a daily necessity for the people and that electricity fees could not be used as a tax standard for permanent expenses. They again requested the municipal government to allow them to cancel it, but were still not approved. The merchants and residents had a case to rely on for the cancellation and were bound to achieve the purpose of cancellation. The situation was already turbulent and imminent. As a result, on the 21st of this month, police officers from the First Police Station clashed with the accountant of the Jiacheng Silver Store when collecting the electricity surcharge. The station charged him with obstructing official duties and sent police officers to arrest and punish the accountant, Fang Changda. Thus, the electricity surcharge turmoil that had been brewing for months broke out from here. When this happened, I was in Chao investigating a case. When I returned to Shantou on the afternoon of the 22nd, I inquired from all parties to find out the truth of the turmoil. At this military period, if the turmoil were to expand, I was sincerely afraid of affecting the security of the rear. Therefore, I and Supervisor Yang Jianping tried our best to mediate and inquire about the intentions of both parties. On the side of the municipal government, if the electricity surcharge was donated to the municipal government's expenses, it could be canceled at any time. On the side of the merchants and residents, if the municipal government's expenses were not as insufficient as the number of finances were public, and the monthly expenses were really insufficient, they would naturally find ways to make up for it. I believe that the key to resolving this case lies in whether or not the political expenses have been settled, and whether or not the turmoil can be quelled lies in whether or not the surcharges can be canceled. However, in this fiery scene, we should first start with canceling the surcharges, and then move on to planning how to make up for the political expenses after the surcharges are canceled. Therefore, on this day, the merchants and residents put forward three requirements and set a compromise method. I and Supervisor Yang were responsible for signing our names as the basis for resolving this case. However, it is easy to cancel the surcharges, but difficult to make up for the political expenses. Whether this case can be completely resolved depends on how to make up for the political expenses after the surcharges are canceled. I think that the merchants and residents intend to predict that the municipal treasury will have surpluses and no deficits, while the municipal government's monthly income and expenditure are not sufficient. It seems that the municipal government might as well make the monthly income and expenditure public so that the people can understand the content of income and expenditure, which is in line with the principle of financial transparency and also demonstrates the rules of official-civil cooperation, so that the municipal treasury has no deficit and the municipal administration has the hope of progress, which would be very good. However, financial transparency cannot be based on empty talk. There should be concrete measures so that merchants and residents can have the opportunity to participate. Now, merchants and residents are requesting the National Government to establish a Shantou Municipal Financial Management Committee, referring to the example of establishing financial management bureaus in various counties. Before the government approves the establishment, it is better for the mayor to clearly and honestly express official-civil cooperation, convene representatives of the Chamber of Commerce to the government to jointly discuss the monthly income and expenditure. On the merchants' and residents' side, the surcharges have been canceled and the income and expenditure situation has been clarified, so they will naturally be happy to raise funds. In this way, the electricity surcharge turmoil, which has lasted for months and almost plunged Shantou into a dangerous situation, can also be brought to an end. All the details of the electricity surcharge turmoil in Shantou and the mediation process between me and Supervisor Yang are hereby reported to your government for review. (June 6th)

Suqian's Hanxu is Captured by Bandits 67

The County Police Force is Weak and Dare Not Advance. Xuzhou Correspondence: Banditry has recently been rampant in the southern part of Suqian. The bandit leader is Liu Rongduo, nicknamed Liu Ershui, who was captured by the county last month and escaped. He has gathered followers and joined forces with the bandit leader Wei San. On the 2nd, they broke through Hanxu, 20 li south of Suqian City. Hanxu is located between the east and west roads, with two fortified villages that are doing well in business and are a prosperous area in the south of the city. The fortified villages are large in the south and small in the north, and their strength is also strong in the south and weak in the north. The southern fortified village has 50 quick-firing guns and is usually heavily guarded, forming a strategic alliance with Yexu and Yangxu. This time, it was captured because bandits first sneaked into the fortified village. Taking advantage of the morning when farmers were busy, they fired guns inside the fortified village, and the bandits outside responded. After Hanxu's southern fortified village was captured, the northern fortified village could not be defended either. The disaster victims there fled south to the Buzi Collection and north to the city to seek safety. After looting Hanxu, the bandits occupied it and forced all the villages, large and small, in the vicinity, such as Zhao Qunqiang and Qin Qunqiang, to evacuate. It is estimated that the area within seven or eight li nearby is a bandit zone. When the county government heard the news, it sent a police brigade to join forces with the militia to suppress them, but due to their weakness, they failed to attack. The fortified villages near Hanxu have also set up defenses to protect themselves. The people are learning the Small Sword Society to protect themselves. Even though the wheat is ripe in the fields, they dare not leave the fortified villages to harvest it. The police team in the city has stepped up its defenses. The Suqian County Party Department urgently telegraphed the Zheng Committee to request that measures be taken to suppress the bandits. The telegram stated: "Bandits are rampant in the southern part of the county. We have repeatedly telegraphed the province to request that measures be taken to suppress them. In the winter, a group of bandits attacked and captured Hanxu and other important towns in the south of Suqian, burning, killing, and looting everything. Refugees have been fleeing to the city to petition, and there are several cases every day. The county team and militia are weak. We are again requesting the provincial government to quickly send heavy troops to suppress the bandits to ensure the safety of the people. Otherwise, we will have no choice but to ask to be dismissed from our posts to apologize to the people of Suqian." (10th)

Problems Arise with the Reorganization of the Anhui Provincial Chamber of Commerce 68

Wuhu Correspondence: The second session of the Anhui Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation Congress has been open for five days and has held four formal meetings. The convocation of this congress to reorganize in accordance with the new Chamber of Commerce Law is also an important issue, as the ministry order stipulates that all chambers of commerce must be reorganized and established before August 15th, otherwise they will lose their qualifications. The congress was originally scheduled to hold elections on the 8th and had already telegraphed the Provincial Party Department and the Provincial Government to send personnel to supervise the elections. However, yesterday, it received a reply from the Provincial Party Department stating that since the county and town chambers of commerce under the Federation had not been organized according to the new law, the Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation could not proceed with the elections immediately and should stop the process. The Provincial Government's reply has not yet been received, so yesterday's election congress was not held and continued to discuss proposals as usual. However, the representatives from various counties must complete the reorganization procedures because they came to Wuhu from afar and are currently planning to proceed. The resolutions passed at the third and fourth congresses are recorded below: Third Congress: 1. The Xiang'an Chamber of Commerce proposed the establishment of a post office in Xiang'an. The resolution was to send a letter to the Anhui Postal Administration requesting the addition of a post office. 2. The Linhuai Chamber of Commerce proposed A, the cancellation of the 50% inland tax. The resolution was to petition the Ministry of Finance to abolish it. B, requested the exemption of local cloth from tax. The resolution was to petition the Anhui Financial Commissioner's Office to exempt it in advance. 3. The Datong Chamber of Commerce proposed A, the establishment of a labor-capital arbitration office. The resolution was to petition the association to establish it. B, requested the amendment of Articles 33 and 34 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Chamber of Commerce Law to protect their status. The resolution was that in addition to the association petitioning for amendments, it should also unite with the provincial chambers of commerce federations in the country to strive for it. 4. The Qiupu Chamber of Commerce proposed A, that the currency system should be unified with silver instead of yuan. The resolution was to ask the National Chamber of Commerce Federation to petition the National Government to reform it. B, requested that the Shanghai tea warehouses be notified to continue to provide samples as usual to avoid exploitation. The resolution was to send a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to notify the tea warehouses to handle it as usual. 5. The Huaiyuan Chamber of Commerce proposed the cancellation of the egg tax in the province. The resolution was to strive for cancellation. 6. The Lujiang Chamber of Commerce proposed that foreign merchants should be prohibited from establishing management offices inland. The resolution was to request the government to strictly prohibit it in accordance with the treaty. 7. The Lu'an Chamber of Commerce proposed requesting the suppression of bandits to ensure commercial security. The resolution was to petition the provincial government and the Anhui Bandit Suppression Headquarters to handle it. 8. The Dangtu County Chamber of Commerce proposed that the stamp tax has many malpractices and is increasingly harassing. The resolution was to send a letter requesting improvements to avoid harming merchants. 9. The Wuhu Tea Merchants proposed that tea leaves are often extorted handling fees when passing through various likin bureaus. The resolution was to send a letter to the Financial Commissioner's Office ordering them to collect taxes in accordance with the regulations and not to extort extra fees. 10. The Xihe Chamber of Commerce proposed the cancellation of likin cards. The resolution was to request the Financial Commissioner's Office to order the immediate cancellation. 11. The Fanchang Chamber of Commerce proposed that, because bandits are rampant, the association should retain the Capital Garrison Regiment stationed in Anhui to suppress the bandits. The resolution was to send a telegram to the General Headquarters to retain them. Fourth Congress: 1. The Bengbu, Mingguang, Shouxian, Sixian, Fengyang and other nine chambers of commerce in northern Anhui proposed A, that Fengguan should be abolished and should not be transferred to the control of the Customs Service. The resolution was to submit separate requests to the National Government, the Ministry of Finance, and the Anhui Provincial Government, striving for the abolition based on the treaty. Before the regular customs is abolished, the name of the supervisor must be restored, and it must not be quickly controlled by the Customs Service by foreigners. B, requested the cancellation of Yao Fang's proposal to the Anhui Provincial Government to establish a public wharf in Anqing, allowing foreign ships to dock and lose navigation rights. The resolution was to submit separate requests to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Communications, and the Provincial Government to immediately cancel Li Fang's proposal and severely punish the proposer. C, proposed to the Provincial Government to fundamentally reorganize Anhui's finances to enrich the provincial treasury. The resolution was to request the Provincial Government to establish a Financial Reorganization Committee and an Audit Committee. (Temporary Motion) 1. The resolution was to promote domestic goods and actively prepare for the establishment of an Anhui Provincial Domestic Goods Exhibition Hall in Wuhu and nominated Chen Zhongyu, Li Zhuxi, Ding Xizhai, Li Yunfeng, Tao Yutang, and She Ceqin as members of the drafting committee. 2. The association's foundation and recurring expenses were resolved to be discussed at the next congress. 3. The report stated that the Beijing side planned to move the Wuhu rice market to Nanjing. If this were to happen, not only would Wuhu's commerce be completely destroyed, but also the counties in Anhui Province would be greatly affected. The resolution was to discuss relief methods at the next congress. 4. The National Goods Company welcomed a visit and adjourned for one day on the 10th. The fifth congress will continue on the 11th.

Su Bingwen Talks About the Situation in Manchuria 69

Harbin Correspondence: Today, Su Bingwen, commander of the Chinese Eastern Railway Defense Army in Harbin, came from Hailar. I interviewed him at the Madier Hotel. According to Su, the Russian military border commander has recently been replaced. Bulkhairyu (i.e., Galen) has been transferred back to Moscow. The main part of the Russian army is located at the Da Wuli headquarters. A small number of troops are stationed at Abahaitu on the Sino-Russian border. The sound of artillery fire can be heard from time to time, which is probably from Russian soldiers practicing. I will take the time to meet with the Russian commander in Da Wuli after my mission in Harbin is completed, because there are many things to be negotiated on the border between the two sides. The 15th Brigade and the 17th Brigade have now been replenished to full strength. Each brigade still has three regiments. One regiment of the 17th Brigade is stationed in Fularji on the Harbin-Manzhouli Line, assisting in guarding the railway. One regiment of the 15th Brigade Infantry and one regiment of the 2nd Cavalry Brigade are stationed in Manzhouli. One regiment of the 15th Brigade Infantry is stationed in the Hinggan Mountains and Hailar. The troops of the 1st Brigade Infantry are stationed from Boketu to Duiaqingshan. In addition, because Russian bandits appear from time to time on the western front, two regiments of troops are dispatched from the 2nd Cavalry Brigade to fill in, with one regiment responsible for suppressing the bandits. In Yakshi and Sanhe Town, White Russians are searched. The White Russians, numbering about one hundred and several tens, are led by Zhai Kuofu, who is pretending to be Seminof to restore the Russian Empire and is calling for the occupation of the Sanhe area and the expansion of the organization. After the 2nd Cavalry Brigade suppressed them, they have been defeated. Zhai Kuofu and his remnants, numbering about thirty or forty, have fled to the grasslands of Inner Mongolia, but these dying embers will soon be completely eliminated. A part of Mongolia is cunning and had previously planned to take advantage of the Russian turmoil to seize control of Hailar's political power. Because the Sino-Russian incident was resolved quickly, these people's plans were not realized. Recently, Inner Mongolian nobles held a joint celebration. I have tried my best to contact their princes and others and have strongly warned the Han people not to enslave the Mongolians, so the relationship between the Han and Mongolians is very harmonious. Commerce in Manzhouli is difficult to restore at the border for a while. Hailar is actively restoring to its original state, which is expected to be not far away. (June 7th) Local correspondence

Songjiang 70

Four People Released in Shenxiang Kidnapping Case: Bandits from the Tianmashan Area of Songjiang County. On the afternoon of the fourth, over forty bandits came to Shenxiang Town to guard the town's outskirts, wantonly searching and looting. Before leaving, they kidnapped Wu Xianglin, Liu Shouzhi, Liu Qitao, Ye Sansheng, and Cheng Musheng, a total of five people. They forced them onto the bandit ship, taking the loot and escaping. Afterwards, the losses from the kidnapping were tallied at two thousand yuan. The county government issued an order to arrest the bandits. It is now known that all the kidnapped individuals except Wu Xianglin have been released. They were confined to the bandit ship for two days and nights, with their eyes blindfolded during the day. The release point was approximately near Fengjing. Currently, the bandit side is demanding seven thousand yuan from Wu's family as ransom, instructing Liu and the others to notify their families to quickly prepare and negotiate. However, Wu Xianglin's family is not wealthy, and the family is at a loss upon hearing this.

Construction Bureau Seeks Labor to Demolish the Moon City: Since the First District Office in the county town began vigorously demolishing Gao Bridge, traffic has greatly improved. However, since the four city moon cities have not yet been demolished, vehicular traffic seems unable to fully pass through. Now, upon receiving an order from the provincial office, the demolition of the moon city has been approved. The Construction Bureau has prepared drawings and plans to announce and seek labor to undertake the project. Bidding is scheduled for the twentieth of this month.

Case of Using Old Stamps Discovered: The Jiaxing Post Office discovered that a letter from this region's Provincial Middle School, signed by Xu Ziyun, contained a method for repeatedly using old stamps. The method involved fully coating the stamp surface with paste. Although the post office had stamped it, the recipient could peel it off, soak it in hot water for a few minutes, and the stamp would fade along with the paste, allowing it to be reused. The Heju Bureau immediately reported this to the General Post Office. Yesterday, the Shanghai General Post Office sent personnel to Songjiang to meet with the Songjiang Local Post Office Director Duan to visit County Magistrate Jin and inquire at the Provincial Middle School. It is said that a student used an alias. This case will be resolved by the Shanghai General Post Office. The student has not been found since leaving the school.

Xu Dingpei, a First-Year Student at the County Middle School, Runs Away: Xu Dingpei of Qibao, a first-year student at the County Middle School, recently took leave after class and went out. Another teacher spotted him and criticized him for leaving the school gate without permission, marking him down with a major demerit. Upon returning to school, the student explained to the teacher that he had previously requested leave from another teacher, protesting the demerit. For some reason, another major demerit was added. The next day, the student secretly left the school and disappeared without a trace. When asked, his family also said he had not returned. Therefore, there is much speculation about the student's whereabouts. He is still nowhere to be found.

Suzhou 71

Headquarters Sends Personnel to Reward Wounded Soldiers: The Headquarters Wounded Soldier Inspection Team sent Qian Weiju, along with Dong Renlin, the Director-General of the Lizhi Society, Deng Shiping, the Deputy Director-General, and others, carrying one thousand yuan to Suzhou to reward wounded soldiers. They first distributed the funds at the Fifteenth Rear Hospital on the afternoon of the previous day (the eleventh). Yesterday (the twelfth), they distributed the funds at the Seventeenth Rear Hospital. Each soldier received ten yuan, each lieutenant-level officer received thirty yuan, and each field-grade officer received fifty yuan. Also, yesterday morning (the twelfth), another one hundred and eighty wounded and sick soldiers arrived in Suzhou from Nanjing for treatment at the Seventeenth Rear Hospital.

Wuxi 72

Wounded Soldiers from the Front Lines Arrive in Wuxi for Treatment: The local county government received an order to establish a rear hospital to receive wounded soldiers. County Magistrate Sun has already sent personnel to Huishan to survey the houses and organize a reception for the wounded soldiers. It is now known that the county government received a telegram from the Ministry of Military Affairs stating that two thousand wounded soldiers would be transported to Wuxi for treatment and instructing them to prepare in advance. It is said that wounded soldiers from the front lines are scheduled to begin arriving in Wuxi in batches starting today (the thirteenth) for treatment. The doctors who will treat the wounded soldiers will also come to Wuxi with the soldiers.

Four Robbers Executed by Firing Squad: On the evening of February 5th of the seventeenth year of the Republic, the No. 6 patrol boat of the 6th Platoon of the 2nd District of the Water Police stationed in the Nanshuangmiao area of the county was suddenly robbed by fourteen bandits wielding guns. Two Mauser rifles and one signal flag were looted. Subsequently, the bandits robbed two businesses in the town, Xue Lixing Rice Store and Yuanfeng Grocery Store. Last year, they also robbed the Youjiatan in Sizhang and the Xiyang Bridge area. Afterwards, police detectives successively apprehended the bandits involved in the case: Yuan Asan, Wu Xirong, Liu Fuyuan, and Wang Hongbao. They were escorted to the county for interrogation, where they all confessed to the robberies. Unexpectedly, on the night of March 26th of this year, the two criminals, Yuan Asan and Wu Xirong, colluded with five other inmates, including Li Chengguo, to break out of jail. On May 9th, Wu Zhengrong, the Chief of Political Police of the County Government, re-arrested Yuan and Wu in Shanghai and sent them back to the county for confinement. Yesterday (the twelfth), the county government received a provincial telegram instructing them to execute the four robbers, including Yuan. County Magistrate Sun immediately dispatched police at 10:00 AM to take the four robbers, including Yuan Asan, from the detention center, verify their identities, bind them, and take them to the South School Field for execution by firing squad.

Large Quantity of Narcotics Robbed: Li Guangde, a well-known dealer in opium and red pills on the roads of this county, purchased seven pieces of red pills, totaling over 70,000 pills and valued at over 400 yuan, in Shanghai the day before yesterday. Yesterday, he secretly transported them to Wuxi by car. He got off the car at the Nanqi Station outside the South Gate. Li immediately instructed his henchmen to carry them, hoping to take them back to his home. Unexpectedly, three or four hooligans found out and immediately followed them. When they reached the railway bridge, they immediately stepped forward and robbed the seven pieces of red pills and fled. Afterwards, Li Guangde knew that they were prohibited items and could only remain silent and regret his actions.

Tragic Accident of a Child Hit by a Train: Yesterday at around 10:00 AM, a train running on the Chang-Hu line heading downwards passed the Yangqi area west of this county's station when a Jiangbei boy, about seven or eight years old, suddenly placed a stone on the track, intending to play a game. Unexpectedly, as he was placing the stone, the train suddenly arrived, and the child was unable to dodge in time, resulting in him being hit in the head by the locomotive. He bled profusely, collapsed in extreme pain, and lost consciousness. The porters at the station spotted this, carried the child to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. It is reported that his injuries are quite serious, and there is concern for his life.

Resolution of Labor-Management Dispute in the Sock Industry: The labor and management sides of the sock industry in Xiyi had a dispute over the revision of the agreement, which had been unresolved for a long time. County Magistrate Sun Zuji specifically convened representatives from both sides of the sock industry, including Wen Zichen and Zhu Fuming, at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss and mediate a resolution. The final resolution was as follows: (1) The management side's deduction of union dues from workers' wages will still be handled in accordance with the agreement, and the latter half of Article 13 of the agreement will be revised to read: "If the management side's deduction is found to be untrue, it will be jointly penalized upon investigation." (2) The labor side, led by the General Labor Union, will publicize the reasons for the management side's deduction of union dues and their uses to workers in various villages. (3) The county government will issue a public notice resolving the sock industry dispute, ordering both parties to comply with the agreement.

Four Robbers Apprehended in Hutang Bridge: Near Hutang Bridge in Wu County, seven robbery cases have occurred continuously since the twentieth.

June 13, 1930 (Shenbao, Third Edition) Recently, the Chamber of Commerce Branch apprehended four robbers, Bao Yu, Li Zhenhai, Cui Lin, and Wang Dezhang, on the night of the tenth, and seized items such as small knives, flashlights, wallets, and pawn tickets. Zhenjiang 74

Measures for Land Consolidation in the Construction Area of the Provincial Capital: The measures for land consolidation in the pilot construction area of the provincial capital, drafted by the Jiangsu Construction Department, were approved at the 301st meeting of the Provincial Government. They are recorded as follows: (1) Landowners within this area must, within two months from the date of the announcement, obtain land registration forms from the Construction Department of the Provincial Capital Construction Engineering Office and fill them out in detail. Those who fail to register within the deadline and do not apply for an extension within the registration period will be deemed to have no owner, and the land will be confiscated for public use. (2) During the two-month registration period, the buying and selling of land and houses and the construction of houses will be temporarily suspended. (3) The grades of each segment and its land price are stipulated as the standard for land collection and return during the land consolidation period. This regulation will be cancelled immediately after the land consolidation in this area is completed. (4) According to the ratio of the total area of roads in this area, the proportion of land to be used for road construction per mu will be calculated, and it will be borne equally per mu. The detailed measures will be stipulated separately. (5) After land consolidation, the Land Bureau will issue new deeds and cancel the old deeds at the same time. (6) Construction of houses must begin within six months from the date of issuance of the new land deed. If the deadline is exceeded, a vacant land tax will be levied, which will be determined separately.

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance Reappoints Financial Bureau Chiefs: Yesterday (the twelfth), the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance reappointed a large number of county financial bureau chiefs. The appointment letters have been issued separately. The county names and surnames are recorded as follows: Yixing Li Jianding, Jurong Hu Longzao, Lianshui Qu Rong, Jingjiang Zhou Shizai, Songjiang Shen Bingchen, Taicang Li Jingmei, Nanhui Wu Benliu, Jiading Yuan Zushen, Piaoshui Zhu Youren, Taixian Huang Xiuyi. In addition, the Department of Finance and the Ministry of Finance's Jiangsu Finance Special Commissioner's Office jointly appointed Zhao Dexin as the director of the Jiangbei Pig Donation Tax Bureau. Zhao has already gone to take office.

The Provincial Party Department Bans the Da Gong Bao: The Jiangsu Provincial Party Rectification Committee saw that Tianjin's Da Gong Bao was being sold by newspaper vendors in this city, with absurd words and false facts. It specifically instructed the county party department to investigate and forward the information to the Provincial Public Security Bureau for strict investigation and prohibition, and sent Wu Xiang to the branch sales office of the newspaper near Jingji Ling to order it to stop distributing.

The Xiang Bao Guard Regiment Meeting Prevents Bandits: The Xiang Bao Guard Regiments in the western region of Zhenjiang held a meeting yesterday after three o'clock to discuss methods for preventing bandits because the bandits have become rampant in the area and have been robbing villages. The results were: (1) When guarding at night, all the guards will gather together to patrol. (2) Those who look suspicious during the day will be strictly interrogated. (3) Each village should prepare more tall lanterns. (4) Sound the gong as a signal when there is an alarm.

Dispute Over Docks Leads to Homicide: Yesterday (the eleventh), two rowing boats on the Zhenjiang River quarreled over docking at the pier, starting with verbal arguments and then resorting to force. Zhao of Boat A struck Wu of Boat B with a hammer. Unexpectedly, the force was too strong, causing Wu's head to be smashed and his brains to spill out. He died on the spot. The water police heard the news, first apprehended Zhao, and then reported to the court for an examination. The murderer was then taken back for punishment.

Yangzhou 75

Faculty and Staff Meeting Discusses the 19th Fiscal Year Budget: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has stipulated that the standard for local education funding budgets for the 19th fiscal year should not exceed 350 yuan per grade per school year for elementary schools and 700 yuan per grade per school year for high schools. Compared with the current education and economic standards in Jiangdu, the budget for each school and grade will be reduced by almost one-third, and the number of faculty and staff will also be reduced by two-fifths. Therefore, faculty and staff at all levels are paying close attention to this matter. If the budget is allocated according to this standard, the monthly income of faculty and staff will not even be comparable to that of the first and second years of the Republic of China, let alone the fact that the cost of living today is ten times that of twenty years ago. This amount is really difficult to maintain. During this time, Director Chen of the Education Bureau has repeatedly requested the county to increase the budget appropriately when he went to the provincial capital to participate in the directors' meeting, so as to avoid being too far from the past facts. The department replied that all directors should follow the department's orders and should not express the impossibility of the situation in advance. Currently, faculty and staff at all schools believe that this matter is of utmost importance. Today (the eleventh), faculty and staff at all levels of each school were summoned to the Public Lecture Hall in Mǎshén Temple to hold an emergency meeting to discuss this matter.

Xu promised to provide relief for the serious disaster of the collapse of the Jiang'an River. Order from the County to Deal with Military Field Case: The Ministry of Military Affairs ordered the county government to quickly implement the procedures for dealing with the case of the Tonghai Reclamation and Animal Husbandry Company's encroachment on the military fields of the Sulzhen and Langshan Battalions, which were approved by the National Government: (1) Pay the silver price within one month. Slaughtering Storm Temporarily Mediated: The Ningbo Municipal Government believes that the outbreak of this slaughtering storm was actually caused by a few large meat shops spreading rumors and causing the shops to strike. The day before yesterday, they specifically summoned representatives of the meat shops in the city to talk, and the Chief of the Health Section, Mao Xian, earnestly advised them of the harm of the strike. After the talks, the meat shops selected three representatives to convene a meeting and respond again. It was also reported that the Ningbo Municipal Government summoned more than 30 meat merchants at 10:00 AM yesterday to discuss the slaughterhouse issue. First, Mao Xian, the Chief of the Health Section, reported the orders and detailed rules of the Ministry. The meat merchants repeatedly stated various grievances and requested: (1) Requesting to add a second slaughterhouse chief. This request still needs to be reported to the mayor. Mao Xian and others will discuss the methods for this request with the mayor. The meat merchants believe that the problem has not been resolved and it is still difficult to start the market.

Bandits Rampage in the Villages West of Yin: In the Xixia Village area near Huang Gulin, west of Yin, lives a Hu widow whose husband, Zhongming, used to do business in Shanghai and had some savings. Unfortunately, he died young, leaving only one son named Yongliang, who is 13 years old. Unexpectedly, six bandits suddenly came the night before last, three of whom each held a white Langlin handgun, crashed through the door, and kidnapped Yongliang and fled west. Also, in the Yangxiakou area of Yinjiang Bridge, west of Yin, the Liang Xingfang family is quite wealthy. Pinghu 80

Cargo Ships Must Light Mast Lights When Sailing at Night: The Inland River Water Police Bureau of this province and the Navigation Bureau recently issued a notice that because inland rivers often have heavy cargo ships carrying stones, coal, etc. sailing at night without lights, collisions and damage to ships often occur with patrol ships. It is ordered that these heavy cargo ships must light mast lights when sailing at night and must give way immediately upon hearing the whistles of ships. Those who cause collisions will be ordered to compensate for repairs.

This County Will Set Up a Court: The High Court recently decided to establish county courts in six counties with more lawsuits, including Tiantai, Yongkang, Xiangshan, Pujiang, Fenghua, and this county. Once the funding is determined, the work will begin and will be completed within this year.

Pinghu Double Pagodas Will Be Repaired Soon: The double pagodas of Pinghu Dezang Temple are said to have been built in the Tang Dynasty. Dai Jitao has previously donated funds and in accordance with the regulations for the preservation of ancient monuments, the demolition proposal was cancelled. The Provincial Government sent Zhang Dinghua, the section chief of the Seventh Section of the Department of Civil Affairs, to Pinghu on the 6th to inspect the site for contracting and estimate prices. It is reported that after County Magistrate Hou received the order from the department, work will begin within two months. First, the east pagoda will be repaired, and then the west pagoda will be repaired. After the repair, the houses under the pagoda will be demolished and surrounded by cement railings to enhance the view. During the pagoda repair period, the county magistrate will be ordered to send police to protect the site.

Letter from the China International Famine Relief Commission 84

Dear Sir/Madam, We have received a letter from the Honolulu Chinese Chamber of Commerce dated May 9, which states: "We read in the Shanghai Shenbao that your commission has temporarily suspended its fundraising and relief efforts due to the unstable political situation. Please confirm if this is true." Our commission has been doing its best to provide relief to the famine in the Northwest, and has spared no effort in providing relief to the provinces of Shaanxi and Gansu. Over the past two years, we have allocated 600,000 yuan to Shaanxi and over 370,000 yuan to Gansu. As for the relief grain transported, even for Shaanxi Province alone, it has reached over 2,200 tons. As for Gansu, due to transportation inconveniences, the amount of grain purchased and distributed locally is not counted. As for the Chinese and Western relief workers sent out, there have been 22 in Shaanxi, including Gao Houru and Li Liangbi, and 4 in Gansu, including An Xianling and Gao Jincheng. Currently, Mr. Baker, the relief director of our commission, is personally stationed in Shaanxi, actively supervising the distribution of emergency relief, hoping to get through the difficult time of the spring famine and then continue to carry out work relief as a permanent solution. Because Shaanxi and Gansu have been suffering from famine for years and the people are not living well, our commission has been doing its best to raise funds and has never stopped. We have always admired your newspaper's wide circulation at home and abroad, and it is enough to influence public opinion. Therefore, we are stating the facts about our commission's recent two years of relief work in Shaanxi and Gansu. If you could disclose this information in your newspaper to show the facts, it would be a favor not only to our commission. China International Famine Relief Commission, June 5, 1930

June 13, 1930 (Republic of China) (Educational News)

News Highlights

Ministry of Education

Meeting to Discuss Promoting Phonetic Symbols 85

In order to actively promote phonetic symbols, the Ministry of Education invited Wu Zhihui to give a lecture at the Ministry of Education at 2:00 PM on the eleventh. All members of the Ministry of Education and guests, including Yang Xingfo of the Academia Sinica, attended. Minister Jiang gave a speech introducing Wu Zhihui. Wu Zhihui's lecture said that the promotion of phonetic symbols should not be seen as difficult. The intellectual class should first learn and teach, and then actively promote them. Then many people can quickly spread the ordinary teachings and promote them easily. Now, let's start with unifying the pronunciation. Add phonetic symbols next to the initial elementary Mandarin textbooks and teach them seriously. If students fail the national phonetic alphabet exam, they will not be allowed to graduate (the speech was very long, and the Ministry of Education Secretary Fang organized it). After the lecture at 3:30, the Ministry of Education invited Wu to be the Chairman of the Standing Committee of the Promotion Committee (Phonetic Symbols). He then took the opportunity to hold a discussion meeting to discuss ways to promote phonetic symbols. The meeting adjourned in the evening.

Provisional Regulations for the Management of Private Schools in Jiangsu 86

The Provisional Regulations for the Management of Private Schools in Jiangsu Province have been passed by the Provincial Government at its 294th meeting and are recorded below:

Article 1: Any educational organization established by a private individual or a private association that cannot fully comply with the current school system but aims to educate children subject to compulsory education shall be considered a private school.

Article 2: Private schools shall comply with the educational aims and implementation policies of the Republic of China, and pay attention to the physical, mental, knowledge, and skill development of the educated.

Article 3: The curriculum of private schools shall be based on the standard of primary schools.

Article 4: Private schools shall be managed by the education committee member of the district where they are located, under the direction of the education bureau director or municipal government of the respective county.

Article 5: Private schools shall be established only in areas more than two li away from existing primary schools or in areas where each class in nearby primary schools already has more than fifty children.

Article 6: The name of a private school shall be the name of the village, alley, street, or neighborhood where it is located, followed by "Private School."

Article 7: The founder of a private school shall prepare a written application for the establishment of the private school, which shall be submitted through the responsible education committee member to the education bureau or municipal government of the respective county for approval and issuance of a private school establishment permit, and shall be reported annually by the education bureau or municipal government to the education department and the county government for record. The format of the application shall be separately determined by the education department. (The founder mentioned in the preceding paragraph includes the school board members who hire teachers and establish schools, as well as the teachers who establish schools themselves.)

Article 8: If a private school violates the provisions of these regulations or does not accept the supervision and guidance of the responsible education committee member, the education bureau or municipal government of the respective county shall immediately take action to rectify the situation.

Article 9: The required subjects in private schools shall be Party Principles, National Language, Arithmetic, General Knowledge, and Physical Education. Elective subjects shall include Music, Art, Work, Agriculture, Commerce, etc.

Article 10: The official teaching materials of private schools shall be limited to textbooks approved by the Ministry of Education. Supplementary materials shall be limited to reading materials designated by the education bureau or municipal government of the respective county.

Article 11: Private schools shall teach Party Principles for one hour per week (divided into three sessions), National Language for twelve hours per week (including speaking, reading, and writing), and allocate a certain number of hours for elective subjects, self-study, and exercise.

Article 12: Private schools shall divide children into four to eight groups based on their level.

Article 13: Private schools shall follow the current academic calendar of the respective county for ceremonies and commemorative days. In addition to Sunday afternoon holidays each week, appropriate holidays may be granted during busy farming seasons, but not exceeding one month within a year. If an infectious disease is prevalent or if a child has contracted an infectious disease, classes shall be suspended at any time.

Article 14: Private school buildings shall pay attention to lighting, ventilation, and appropriate humidity. Playgrounds may utilize shaded courtyards. Toilets must be designated and hygiene must be observed.

Article 15: Private school equipment shall include the Party and National flags, a portrait of Sun Yat-sen, a blackboard, chalk, a duster, textbooks, teachers' guides, dictionaries, water bottles, daily schedules, attendance books, student registers, grade books, writing brushes, ink stones, rags, spittoons, etc., all of which shall be purchased by the founder of the private school.

Article 16: In addition to complying with the provisions of Article 5, private schools shall not admit children who have attended primary school but have not graduated.

Article 17: The names of children enrolled in and withdrawn from private schools shall be submitted annually in a list by the responsible education committee member to the education bureau or municipal government of the respective county for record.

Article 18: All teachers in private schools must be registered and certified by the education bureau or municipal government of the respective county. The registration and certification procedures shall be separately determined by the education department.

Article 19: The tuition fees charged by teachers who establish private schools themselves shall be determined by the county education bureau, taking into account local conditions, and submitted to the education department for approval.

Article 20: The performance of private school teachers and children shall be examined by the responsible education committee member and submitted in a list to the education bureau or municipal government of the respective county for record.

Article 21: Private schools that meet the following conditions may, in accordance with the regulations for private schools, be submitted by the education bureau or municipal government to the education department for registration as private elementary schools:

(1) The subjects and equipment are completely consistent with those of elementary schools.

(2) The teachers have passed the elementary school teacher certification examination.

(3) The school has been inspected by provincial and county school inspectors or education committee members more than twice a year and is considered to have excellent performance.

Article 22: All previous private school regulations, measures, and orders promulgated by this province and various counties before the promulgation of these regulations shall be repealed.

Article 23: These regulations shall be resolved by the Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee, promulgated and implemented, and reported to the Ministry of Education for record.

City Education Bureau Actively Preparing for the Joint Examination 87

The City Education Bureau is sparing no effort in preparing for the joint examination for primary and secondary schools. Registration of the College of Law and Political Science of China Public School 92

The Ministry of Education has recently approved the registration of China Public School and its College of Law and Political Science in Shanghai. However, upon review, China Public School is an independent college in nature, and is equivalent to an independent college in terms of the academic system. It should receive the same treatment as an independent college. Therefore, the school's original College of Arts and Sciences should be renamed the College of Arts and Sciences, the College of Social Sciences should be renamed the College of Law and Commerce, and the College of Pre-Medical Studies should be renamed the Affiliated High School.

Twenty-one to nine.

Guangdong First Women's Normal School and Liangjiang basketball teams met at the China Basketball Room last night at 7:00 PM. After a fierce battle, Liangjiang finally won with a score of 21 to 9. In the second half, the fighting between the two armies gradually weakened, and the situation was more harmonious, and fewer points were scored. The result was 21 to 9, and Liangjiang won. Looking at the overall game yesterday, Liangjiang's basketball skills can be said to have greatly improved. The coordination between the forwards and defenders was quite flexible. Jinan Advocates Physical Education 99

Has practical methods that can be used as a model for various schools. Zhongwai News Agency said that our country's athletes suffered a disastrous defeat in this Far East Games. Although there is more than one reason for this, it is difficult to deny that the backwardness of technology is a difficult matter. The National Jinan University in West Shanghai has always been known in society for its expertise in sports. After suffering this setback, the athletes who returned did not feel discouraged. They believed that there was no way to improve in technology without applying scientific methods. The school authorities believed that many of the students in the school were descendants of overseas Chinese, and their physical qualities were generally excellent. The youth with excellent physical qualities were also excellent materials. Teaching students according to their aptitude is a good opportunity and place to create sports talents. The relationship between the Far East and the country's reputation is the responsibility of every man, and there is no room for complacency. The school has already formulated a great plan to implement vigorously. The investigation is recorded as follows: (1) Hiring Germans to guide and asking Mr. Buqi, the German coach of Northeast University, to be responsible for introducing a German with high technical skills, solid theoretical knowledge, and rich teaching experience to guide the school. The school is willing to make compromises and save money in other aspects, and it will not hesitate to spend a lot of money to recruit this person. (2) Establish a sports department in order to concentrate talents, train them, and create excellent sports teachers for foreign countries. Whether the establishment of the department belongs to the Education College or is directly under the Sports Committee is still being considered. The preparation period is one year, and it is decided to open it in the summer of next year. Its characteristics lie in the use of new methods, with equal emphasis on academic and technical subjects, to correct the theoretical and technical weaknesses of other university sports departments. (3) Funding for overseas students, selecting graduates with excellent grades and good sports skills to send to Europe and the United States to study sports. After completing their studies, they must return to the school to serve for at least three years. During the service period, they will be given a reasonable salary and labor. It must be of an obligatory nature, and special chapters will be formulated separately. (4) Construction of the sports area. The school's sports area was planned long ago, but the progress was delayed due to funding issues. Since the 19th year, the school affairs meeting has decided to treat the sports fees as special accounting and not mix them with regular expenses. Now the school has allocated special funds to rush the construction of the fitness room, Tai Chi room, and swimming pool in the area, and to install a broadcast radio station, which will broadcast the sports results to the outside world at any time, so that the people of the country have instructions and warnings. (5) Conduct compulsory sports. The school does not ask for special and general standards. It now stipulates that each college must hold a sports meeting for teachers and students once each semester, and each person must participate in at least one item. Even those without a special skill must join the health competition invented by Mr. Chu Minyi. In short, the school's striving for strength and ambition is nothing more than to awaken the people of the country and lead the people of the country through sports. I hope that the people of the whole country will rise up and catch up with this spirit. Why is it difficult to wash away the shame? Please look at the Far East four years later. Who will win the championship?

Local News

Abolition of Lijin Committee

Soliciting Post-Abolition Measures 101

The National Abolition of Lijin Conference called by the Ministry of Finance, which is mostly sponsored by consumption tax and business tax, has not yet been officially convened, but the preparatory meeting has been held several times under the chairmanship of Counselor Li. The purpose of the Ministry of Finance in calling this meeting is to plan for post-abolition measures, that is, what methods will be used to offset the national treasury income after the lijin is abolished. Therefore, opinions are currently being solicited for post-abolition measures. In recent days, many provincial financial officials and experts have proposed concrete methods, mostly advocating the implementation of special business consumption tax, business tax, income tax, and other taxes. According to some people's consideration, income tax is difficult to audit and the procedures are cumbersome, so it is temporarily inconvenient to implement. However, consumption tax and business tax will definitely become a reality in the future.

Jianghai Customs

Strictly Investigating Copper Exports 102

Jianghai Customs has previously received an order from the Ministry of Finance to investigate and prohibit the export of copper to Japan, which has been officially announced and strictly enforced. However, villains only know how to seek profit and disregard laws and regulations. In recent days, there have still been private smuggling attempts, especially in large quantities of copper coins. Therefore, starting from today, capable customs officers will be assigned to board all foreign ships sailing from Shanghai to Nagasaki to conduct strict investigations. In addition, the Chinese Consul in Nagasaki will pay close attention to the investigation. It is also reported that Japan has recently requested China to stop the shipment of copper coins. It is heard that the Nagasaki authorities have already discovered the secret shipment of Chinese copper into the country. The Japanese authorities have contacted the Chinese Consul in Nagasaki and asked us to formally issue an order prohibiting the shipment of copper to Japan.

After Gold is Expensive and Silver is Cheap

The Attitude of the Gold Exchange 104

There is a rumor that the Gold Exchange will temporarily close down due to the gold surge. However, Mr. Wei Gongsong, an employee of the exchange, told others that the reason for the gold surge and silver cheapness has been seen in the major newspapers in Shanghai. As for the temporary suspension here, it is not accurate. However, since the occurrence of this trend, the exchange has held several meetings to discuss rescue measures. At the same time, the chairman of the board, Mr. Xu Busun, has repeatedly consulted with Minister Song and Minister Kong on the measures. If it can save the overall situation, the exchange is also happy to temporarily suspend. After all, the power to manipulate this matter lies in foreign banks. The exchange has always been a free market, and its price fluctuations must be sought from foreign exchange rates.

Survey of Rice Crop Stem Borer Damage in Various Districts 110

A Reduction of 151,900 Piculs; Total Losses Exceeding 910,000 Yuan. In recent years, stem borer damage has been severe, causing losses to rice crops. According to a survey by the Entomology Bureaus of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Jiangxi provinces, Jiangsu suffered losses of 10,000 yuan in 1929, Zhejiang suffered losses of 40,000 yuan, and Jiangxi suffered a total loss of 190,000 yuan in 1928 and 1929. The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has ordered municipal commissioners in various districts to select five locations in each area and dig up ten rice roots per location, for a total of fifty roots, to be sent to the bureau for inspection and investigation. The results of the survey show that among a total of 3,299 rice roots, 716 contained stem borers, with a damage rate of 21.7%. The number of rice roots without stem borers was 2,583, accounting for approximately 78.3%. The area of rice paddies in Shanghai is estimated to be 140,000 mu, based on 2/10 of the total area. Assuming a yield of five piculs per mu, the annual rice production would originally be 700,000 piculs. Assuming a damage rate of 21.7% due to stem borers, the reduction in yield would be 151,900 piculs. Assuming the lowest price of six yuan per picul, the total loss would reach over 910,000 yuan. According to the table below, the areas with the highest degree of damage are Yangsi, Jiangwan, Gaohang, Pusong, Yinhang, and Caojing, followed by Zhenru, Gaoqiao, Lihang, Wusong, Tangqiao, and Pengpu. The highest damage rate is 44%, and the lowest is 10%. The table below shows the comparison of stem borer damage levels in various districts of Shanghai in 1929:

Comparison Table of Stem Borer Damage Levels in Various Districts of Shanghai in 1929 (Percentage)

| District | Number of Rice Roots | Number of Roots with Stem Borers | Number of Roots Without Stem Borers | Percentage of Roots Damaged by Stem Borers | Percentage of Roots Not Damaged |

|---|---|---|---|---|---|

| Zhenru | 344 | 66 | 278 | 19.19 | 80.81 |

| Yangsi | 370 | 164 | 206 | 44.05 | 55.95 |

| Tangqiao | 265 | 45 | 220 | 17.00 | 83.00 |

| Lihang | 236 | 27 | 209 | 11.70 | 88.30 |

| Jiangwan | 225 | 64 | 161 | 28.44 | 71.56 |

| Wusong | 319 | 36 | 283 | 11.29 | 88.71 |

| Gaoqiao | 276 | 15 | 261 | 5.22 | 94.78 |

| Gaohang | 241 | 65 | 176 | 27.00 | 73.00 |

| Pusong | 354 | 80 | 274 | 22.60 | 77.40 |

| Caojing | 350 | 68 | 282 | 19.43 | 80.57 |

| Pengpu | 150 | 15 | 135 | 10.00 | 90.00 |

County Magistrate Urges Land Registration 111

The Shanghai County Government previously received instructions from the Department of Finance to conduct land registration, which was forwarded to the Finance Bureau for implementation. However, since the commencement of the process on February 10th of this year, only a small number of people in various districts have complied. The main reason is that many of the land deeds held by the public are old unregistered deeds, and they fear being fined. Therefore, they are all waiting and watching. County Magistrate Yan believes that land registration is designed to protect the property rights of the people and should be actively applied for. It is unreasonable to remain uninformed. With the deadline set by the Department of Finance in June approaching, the registration should be completed as soon as possible. Therefore, in addition to submitting the matter to the county administrative meeting for deliberation, he specially instructed the district chiefs yesterday to expedite the process and not delay further, and to report on the progress of compliance for verification.

Baoshan Finance Bureau Urges Payment of Arrears in Grain Tax 112

Bei Jietai, the director of the Baoshan County Finance Bureau, has found that the amount of arrears in grain tax in the county is very large. With the province and department urging payment, and the local government in urgent need of funds, it is imperative to collect the arrears. Therefore, at 2 p.m. yesterday, he summoned the tax collection officials from the five districts of the county and instructed them to collect the old arrears of busy season grain and unpaid mu tax from the 1927 and 1928 years, requiring all grain handlers to clear them all within half a month. For the 1929 busy season grain, it is even more important to inform all households in arrears to go to the counter to clear them as soon as possible. For those who are stubborn, they are allowed to report the worst cases for detention and forced payment. All old arrears of busy season grain from 1927 that have been incorporated into the urban area should also be strictly pursued. A notice has been issued to urge payment, and the original tax collection officials have been instructed to be responsible for the pursuit of the arrears for disbursement. Furthermore, the Baoshan County Finance Bureau and the Eighth District Party Department of Wusong jointly issued a notice yesterday to clarify the misunderstanding regarding the exemption of the 1927 busy season grain tax.

Japanese Exports to China Decrease 114

A Comparative Decrease of Over 16 Million Yuan. According to a survey report by the commercial officials of the Japanese Embassy in China, the detailed statistics of Japanese imports and exports to China in May (including Kwantung and Hong Kong) through the six major ports of Yokohama, Kobe, Osaka, Nagasaki, Moji, and Hakodate are as follows: Exports amounted to 31,227,000 yuan, and imports amounted to 21,505,000 yuan, with a total of 52,732,000 yuan. The surplus of exports over imports was 9,722,000 yuan. Compared to the same period last year, exports decreased by 16,007,000 yuan, while imports decreased by only 2,079,000 yuan. Furthermore, the total exports from January to May this year amounted to over 27,398,000 yuan, a decrease of 25,744,000 yuan compared to the same period last year. Published by the Municipal Government.

Registration Rules for Industrial and Commercial Organizations 115

As the reorganization of industrial and commercial organizations in Shanghai nears completion, many have applied for registration. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has submitted a request to the Municipal Government for the promulgation of registration rules, which are excerpted as follows:

Article 1: All legally organized industrial and commercial organizations within the municipality must apply to the Social Affairs Bureau for registration in accordance with these rules to receive protection.

Article 2: Those initiating the organization of industrial and commercial organizations, after obtaining permission from the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department to establish an organizing committee, should immediately prepare an application signed by the initiators, a resume of the preparatory committee members, and submit the permit from the Municipal Party Department, the seal of the preparatory committee, and other documents to the Social Affairs Bureau for registration.

Article 3: Industrial and commercial organizations should complete their organization within three months after the preparatory committee is registered. When the Municipal Party Department deems the organization sound, all officers should prepare a signed application, attach two copies each of the articles of association, a list of members (i.e., a list of companies and firms in the same industry, and the names of their business owners or managers), resumes of officers, and various survey forms. They should also submit the Municipal Party Department's approval order certifying the soundness of the organization to the Social Affairs Bureau for registration.

Article 4: The articles of association of industrial and commercial organizations should specify the following: (1) Name and nature of business; (2) Purpose and functions; (3) Region and location; (4) Organization and election/removal of officers; (5) Regulations regarding meetings; (6) Regulations regarding admission, withdrawal, and expulsion of members; (7) Regulations regarding the raising of funds and their income and expenditure methods; (8) Methods of punishment other than expulsion for those who violate the articles of association; (9) Duration of the organization; (10) Regulations regarding dissolution and liquidation.

Article 5: If an industrial and commercial organization fails to complete its organization and apply for registration within three months after the preparatory committee is registered, the Social Affairs Bureau may revoke its registration and ban it.

Page 14

The Sixth Article of the Thirteenth Day of June, Year Nineteen of the Republic of China (Fourth Page of the Shen Bao) Friday (14): After the Social Affairs Bureau approves the registration of an industrial and commercial organization, it should immediately issue a registration certificate and seal, and announce it publicly. Article 7: After an industrial and commercial organization is approved for registration, it should submit the following items to the Social Affairs Bureau for review and record each year: (1) Changes in membership; (2) Work progress; (3) Property status and budget/final accounts; (4) Business operating results; (5) Whether there are any disputes and the process or results of the facts; (6) Temporary or regularly issued printed materials. Article 8: If an industrial and commercial organization needs to amend its regulations after registration, it should submit two copies to the Social Affairs Bureau for approval and record for it to take effect. Article 9: If an industrial and commercial organization has any of the following circumstances after registration, it should report it to the Social Affairs Bureau ten days in advance for approval and record: (1) Date of the general meeting; (2) Re-election of officers; (3) Change of property; (4) Fundraising; (5) Application for liquidation; (6) Reorganization or dissolution of the organization. Article 10: After an industrial and commercial organization is reorganized or dissolved, it should immediately return the registration certificate and seal, and the Social Affairs Bureau will announce it publicly. Article 11: The Social Affairs Bureau should report the matters handled in accordance with the provisions of Articles 6 and 10 above to the Municipal Government for forwarding to the various industrial and commercial departments for record. Article 12: These rules may be amended from time to time if there are any matters not covered. Article 13: These rules shall take effect from the date of promulgation by the Special Municipal Government. May.
