Exchange Bureau Cracks Down on Illegal Transactions 117

A Conversation with a Certain Official of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. The Guowen News Agency reports that the yarn and cloth exchange posted a notice yesterday, which stated: “The Exchange Law and its implementing regulations have been promulgated by the National Government and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and have been ordered by the National Government to take effect simultaneously from June 1st of this year. In addition to sending the law and its implementing regulations to the Brokers Association for their reference, this Exchange must clearly announce them for compliance. According to the law and its implementing regulations, all exchange brokers and commission brokers have an obligation to comply. In particular, Article 29 of the implementing regulations (the notification of a broker's buying, selling, and delivery activities on the exchange shall not take effect unless it is stamped and certified by the exchange to which the broker belongs) has a significant relationship with brokers and commission brokers, and must be given special attention. The facilities of this Exchange have always placed great importance on the status of brokers. All matters concerning the interests of brokers that are observed by this Exchange are announced in a timely manner as a precautionary measure. According to this Exchange's observation of this article, the government's intention in establishing this article is that transactions that are not stamped and certified by the Exchange are actually related to the profits and losses of the Exchange's tax revenue. Furthermore, it is feared that once a dispute arises in such transactions, there is no legal basis and no legal remedy can be obtained. Therefore, in order to prevent all disputes and maintain commercial stability, it is necessary to specifically establish this article to show sanctions. Regardless of whether this legislative intention considers social order, merchant ethics, or national tax revenue, it is also of great benefit to the status of brokers and clients. If brokers and clients can strictly abide by the provisions of this article and earnestly fulfill their obligations, not only can all dangers and malpractices in transactions be eliminated, but also the transactions they carry out will have a legal basis. Even if a dispute occurs, it is not difficult to seek legal remedies in accordance with the law. As for those who only seek petty convenience and engage in illegal activities, is the benefit or harm not clearly distinguishable? For this reason, in addition to requesting that everyone abide by the law and its implementing regulations, we also hope that special attention will be paid to this article.” In addition to notifying the Brokers Association, this announcement is hereby made. After reading it, the reporter finally understood the intention of the Exchange, which was to make it so that notifications of buying and selling parties would not take effect unless they were stamped and certified by the Exchange. However, the essence of the country's legislation was not clearly elaborated. Therefore, the reporter visited a certain official of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for further details. The official made the following statement: (hereinafter, the official's statement) “Although the former Beijing government promulgated the Securities Exchange Law and the Commodity Exchange Regulations, they were brief and riddled with loopholes, which led to abuses that violated the special permits for establishment and prevented the effectiveness of legislation from being realized. The National Government, in view of this, has re-enacted the Exchange Law and its implementing regulations. This is truly a measure by the Central Government to actively rectify industrial and commercial laws and regulations and forcefully correct past malpractices. It has been clearly promulgated and will take effect from June 1st of this year. The most important point is the strict regulation regarding the crackdown on illegal transactions, which is intended to restrict and avoid danger. In the past, the purchase and sale notification letters given by the brokers of various exchanges to the clients on both sides of the transaction (commonly known as the "deal slip") were often not stamped and certified by the exchange, which, from a fundamental point of view, violated the provisions of the current laws and regulations, which is called illegal. In fact, this can evolve into the following abuses, which is called an illegal result: (A) If the transactions made by the broker are not stamped and certified by the exchange to which they belong, then the income from their handling fees will inevitably be reduced. This, from the perspective of the exchange, is harmful and not beneficial. (B) The broker hopes to obtain the handling fee exclusively, and the transactions are not done through proper procedures. From the point of view of profit, there is the possibility of evading exchange fees. From the point of view of harm, if a dispute or loss occurs in the transaction, the client completely denies it, and there is no way to properly resolve the matter. This, from the perspective of the broker, is more harmful than beneficial. (C) If the transaction notification letter has not been legally certified, if the transaction is profitable but the broker completely embezzled it, the client has no legal procedure to prove it and no legal remedy. This, from the client's perspective, is unprofitable and harmful. (D) Since the broker evades the exchange's handling fees, the exchange's income will inevitably decrease, and the exchange tax that the state should collect will also be eroded invisibly. This has a great impact from the perspective of the country. The above four items are based on observations from all aspects, and the abuses can be seen immediately. As for other indirect impacts such as merchant ethics, commercial credit, and social stability, all have a great relationship. In order to avoid the above-mentioned abuses, it is necessary to adopt a strict doctrine and actively crack down on them, showing remedial methods and giving appropriate punishments. This is also a kind of method of the country to promote laws and regulations to eliminate malpractices. In the end, the responsibility of our people lies in following the laws and regulations, and how dare we hesitate and be complacent. We will specifically inform you of the provisions in the Exchange Law and its implementing regulations regarding the crackdown on illegal transactions: Article 50 of the Exchange Law: Those who engage in transactions outside the exchange based on the market price of the exchange and speculate on profits and losses in empty transactions shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to one year or a fine of up to three thousand yuan. Article 29 of the implementing regulations: The notification of a broker's buying, selling, and delivery activities on the exchange shall not take effect unless it is stamped and certified by the exchange to which the broker belongs. Judging from the previous article, illegal transactions without legal procedures not only have the loss of fines but also have criminal responsibility. Exchange brokers and clients on both sides of the transaction should be aware of this, even if they are not considering the country's tax collection, but only considering their own interests, and know that the notification letter must have the stamp and certification of the exchange. In the past, a certain broker in the Japanese transaction department delivered a notification letter that had not been stamped and certified by the transaction department to the client. Afterwards, the broker had accumulated huge assets and resigned from his position for more than ten years. Suddenly, the client sued him, saying that the transaction was illegal. As a result, the broker lost the lawsuit and paid 200,000 yuan in damages to the plaintiff and the transaction department. It can be seen that illegal behavior not only bears the blame at the time but can also be investigated afterwards. We must not try it.”

After listening to this conversation, the reporter of the Guowen News Agency asked if it could be disclosed. Fortunately, it was approved, and the reporter took his leave.

City Gazette Office Organizational Regulations 121

Regulations stipulating standards for the selection of compilers. Since the Shanghai City Gazette Office was entrusted by the City Government to the Director of the Education Bureau, Chen Dezheng, the Director of the Social Bureau, Pan Gongzhan, and Advisor Tang Naikang to prepare, the organizational regulations of the City Gazette Office and the standards for the selection of compilers have been drafted and submitted to the City Government for approval and promulgation. The articles of the regulations are now recorded as follows:

City Gazette Office Organizational Regulations

Article 1: This office is organized in accordance with Article 22 of the "Essentials of Local Gazette Compilation" promulgated by the National Government. It is under the jurisdiction of the Shanghai Special City Government and handles the compilation of the Shanghai Special City Gazette.

Article 2: This office shall have one Director who shall be responsible for all affairs of the office.

Article 3: This office shall have one Deputy Director who shall assist the Director in handling office affairs.

Article 4: This office shall have three permanent compilers and twelve compilers who shall assist the Director and Deputy Director in managing compilation affairs.

Article 5: This office shall have sixteen assistant compilers who shall assist in compilation affairs.

Article 6: This office shall have twenty-four interviewers who shall assist in collection matters.

Article 7: This office may, depending on the complexity of the work, establish ten office staff and employees.

Article 8: The Director, Deputy Director, and compilers of this office shall be appointed by the City Government; the assistant compilers shall be hired by this office; and other personnel shall be appointed or hired by this office.

Article 9: The rules of procedure for meetings of this office shall be formulated separately.

Article 10: The detailed rules of procedure for this office shall be formulated separately.

Article 11: These regulations may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered.

Article 12: These regulations shall come into effect on the date of promulgation by the Shanghai Special City Government.

Standards for the Selection of Gazette Office Compilers

(1) Compilers for the Gazette Office are not limited by origin. Anyone with one of the following qualifications may be appointed:

(A) Those who have insightful views on local gazettes.

(B) Those who are well-versed in specialized academics.

(C) Those who are familiar with the local history of this city.

(2) Those whose statements are erroneous and who are suspected of being counter-revolutionary, even if they meet the above standards, shall not be appointed as

Compilers or Assistant Compilers of the Gazette Office.

The Preparatory Committee of the City Gazette Office held its fourth regular meeting on the afternoon of the 12th. Tang Naikang, Pan Gongzhan, Chen Dezheng, and other three people were present. Chen Dezheng chaired the meeting, and Chen Duanzhi recorded the meeting. The following cases were resolved:

(1) The budget proposal of this committee (Resolution): Amended and passed.

(2) The detailed rules for interviewing for the City Gazette (Resolution): Amended and passed.

(3) The methods for soliciting reference books for the City Gazette Office (Resolution): Amended and passed.

(4) Recommendation of candidates for Director to facilitate the early opening of the office and compilation (Resolution): Passed.

(5) Finding a site for the City Gazette Office (Resolution): Publicly elected Committee Member Chen to be responsible for contacting.

Appeal for Disaster Relief in Shaanxi and Henan 124

The disaster situation in Shaanxi and Henan provinces is expanding. The Shanghai Office of the Disaster Relief Committee received a telegram yesterday from Mr. Li Zushen of the Tianjin Shaanxi Disaster Relief Association, stating that he had received a telegram from Mr. Zhu Ziqiao, reporting that the disaster areas in Shaanxi were again suffering from epidemics. Counties such as Xianyang, Xingping, and Liquan were all suffering from barren fields and villages in ruins. The disaster victims were only able to fill their hunger with a small amount of millet mixed with wild vegetables. The elderly and weak were turning to ravines, and the situation was extremely tragic. Emergency relief is currently being carried out rapidly. Although donations from Tianjin are very enthusiastic, they are a drop in the bucket and cannot make up for the loss. The Shanghai area, known as a wealthy area, has many more philanthropists. Please advocate for the rapid raising of large amounts of funds. The disaster victims will be very grateful. Another telegram was received from the Henan Provincial Relief Association, stating that the southeast of Henan was a war zone, and more than ten counties, including Gong, Deng, Qin, and Wen, had suffered from hailstorms, and the wheat harvest was wiped out, and it was difficult to plant grains again. The starving people were about to have no food to eat. They begged for special relief to be provided, and the merit would be immeasurable. It is reported that the Chairman of the Relief Committee, Xu Jingren, and the Director of the Shanghai Office, Wang Yiting, have decided to request the government to allocate funds for relief and to raise funds for emergency relief in the two provinces. All types of materials, food, and medicine are needed. It is reported that the Shanghai Office has received a lot of relief funds and combined Sharen medicinal water in the past few days.

Suqian Suffers Heavy Disaster, Begs for Relief 125

The Chinese Jisheng Association has repeatedly received telegrams and letters from various agencies in Suqian County, Jiangsu Province, and from the disaster relief committees in various bandit-affected areas, including county gentry Liu Junhongyun and others, reporting that the county suffered a severe flood last year, which caused a complete loss of the wheat crop and a complete failure of the autumn harvest. The disaster situation is serious and in urgent need of rescue. The most tragic situation is that a large number of bandits fled from Suijing into the western part of Suqian, to the Yiyong Town, where they burned, killed, looted, and did everything. Dozens of villages, such as Caizhuang, Yanwan, Xixiaozhuang, and Dawangmiao, were all damaged. It is estimated that more than two hundred people were injured, one hundred and sixty people were kidnapped, and countless houses were burned down. To the south, the areas of Caiwei and Sanjietang were occupied by bandits. Although the troops attacked and suppressed the bandits, who fled, they burned and killed more than 800 households along the way. Furthermore, the whole town of Zhatang Jinzhai Town was burned down, and more than 1,000 people were killed. It was truly an unprecedented catastrophe. The poorest people who have suffered the most are exposed to the elements day and night, starving and waiting to die. The cries of women and children are unbearable to hear. They ask for speedy relief, and the merit will be immeasurable. The county has suffered both natural disasters and banditry, and the situation is truly unbearable. The Association has just completed emergency relief work in Baoying and Huaiyin counties in Jiangsu Province, but the natural disasters and banditry in Suqian have come again, and the vastness of the catastrophe is truly unthinkable.

News on the Meiya Silk Factory Labor Strike Yesterday 126

After the labor strike occurred in the main, fourth, and sixth factories of the Meiya Silk Factory in this port, the City Social Bureau convened representatives of the factory and the employers yesterday for a round of mediation. Because the employers' attitude was tough, the mediation failed to make progress. The City Social Bureau had no choice but to instruct the labor representatives to return to the factory and persuade the workers to resume work first and wait for mediation. After the representatives returned to the factory, they immediately convened a meeting of all the workers and persuaded them to resume work. However, the workers believed that the employers had no sincerity in accepting mediation, and all the workers vowed not to resume work. The representatives were unable to obtain any results and had to request the City Social Bureau to send personnel for mediation again.

Recent News on the Case of the Appeal to Repair the Tang Pagodas in Western Zhejiang 127

The Zhejiang West Tang Dynasty Baoxing Twin Pagodas, since someone hoped to demolish and sell them, have been opposed by the Pinghu fellow villagers in Shanghai and by the gentry in Beijing, Hangzhou, and the local area. Letters and telegrams have been sent to all levels of government. First, the Ministry of Interior ordered an investigation, followed by instructions from the Zhejiang Civil Affairs Department to the Pinghu County Magistrate not to demolish them without authorization. However, the County Magistrate vaguely reported to the Civil Affairs Department, claiming that they were extremely dangerous and contained other untrue statements. After receiving the report, the Zhejiang Civil Affairs Department, believing that it was unreasonable, specially sent Zhang Dinghua, a staff member of the Seventh Section, to the site to climb the pagoda and push it. However, it did not move at all, as the County Magistrate had claimed that it swayed in the wind. Therefore, he re-examined the North Temple with the County Magistrate. As a result, they advocated repairing the pagoda and made an agreement with the local people who advocated repairing the pagoda, stipulating that work must begin within two months to avoid delays. The original agreement is now recorded as follows:

Agreement signed by Shen Songqing and others. The reason for the agreement is that the Baoxing Twin Pagodas built in the Tang Dynasty in front of the Beisi Temple in the county seat of Pinghu have been in disrepair for many years, and the wind and rain have eroded them, posing a danger. Songqing and others, in order to preserve the antiquities, have decided to repair them and have already prepared the estimated costs for the project and submitted them to the Civil Affairs Department for approval. However, it is heard that many local people are advocating for their demolition. Now, with the approval of the committee members, Songqing has made an agreement that if the order from the Civil Affairs Department is received, work must begin to repair them within two months. If the work has not started after two months, the county government and various legal entities may discuss their demolition, and no further objections will be raised. The method of repair is agreed upon as follows:

(1) Songqing and others, in order to preserve the antiquities, have decided to repair the Tang Pagodas. The ruins of the North Temple are numerous and require a large amount of labor. The repair of the halls is not included.

(2) When repairing the twin pagodas, the county government and various legal entities must convene a meeting to discuss how to collect funds and broaden the benefits. The people who advocate repairing the pagoda are naturally the preparation committee members.

(3) When repairing the twin pagodas, an engineer with architectural knowledge from Shanghai must be hired to repair them using scientific methods.

(4) The foundation of the twin pagodas must be solidified with concrete, and the body and top of the pagodas must be supported by steel bones.

(5) After the twin pagodas are repaired, they must not lose their original appearance in order to preserve the original meaning of the antiquities.

(6) After the twin pagodas are repaired, the Civil Affairs Department should be requested to order the demolition of the two small houses next to the pagoda, which are managed by the county education association's property association, and establish a stone railing around the pagoda to enhance the appearance and protect the antiquities.

The agreement is true. Agreement signed by Shen Songqing, Zhang Fuhou, Ran Rongqing, Cheng Jun, Xue Zhenji, Mo Xiangji, Zhao Lin, Ge Changmei, Feng Hao, and Committee Member Zhang Dinghua on June 8th, the 19th year of the Republic of China.

Republic of China 19th Year, Shanghai News 2

French Concession Police Detectives

Rescue of Suzhou Kidnapped Victims 130

Yuan Wenmei Crying All the Way

Xiaobang Bay Head Hides the Kidnapped Victims

The Life and Death of Two Kidnapped Victims is Unknown

The Fugitive Bandits are Being Closely Pursued

At 9:15 last night, a Chinese police officer, number 472, of the French Concession Police was patrolling near the intersection of Avenue de la Grandiere and Rue Massenet when he suddenly saw a boy, about ten years old, wearing a willow-colored cloth short shirt and trousers, running towards him in a panic, staggering, and crying as he ran. He kept looking back as if he was afraid that someone would be chasing him from behind. The police officer was suspicious and stopped him to inquire. As soon as the child saw the police officer, he immediately stopped crying and spoke in the Wujiang dialect. He told the police officer that he had been kidnapped by bandits from Suzhou and hidden in a nearby bungalow in Shanghai for ten days. Because the bandits were all asleep, he was able to take the opportunity to escape from the bandit den and asked for help. The police officer, knowing that he was a kidnapped victim, immediately took him to the Lujiiawan Police Station. The chief of detectives was afraid that the bandits would escape upon hearing the news, so he did not have time to question the kidnapped victim. He immediately used the telephone to notify the Special Agency of Avenue Joffre to gather Chinese and foreign detectives, all wearing steel bulletproof vests and carrying weapons, and travel in cars. They first arrived at the main police station to meet the kidnapped victim and Chinese police officer number 472, and then drove straight to the Xiaobang Bay area of Avenue de la Grandiere and Rue Massenet. The kidnapped victim identified the location clearly, and the detectives rushed in and captured two people on the spot. No pistols were found. They were immediately taken into the police station. After the chief of detectives questioned them one by one, both bandits claimed to be from Anhui. According to the kidnapped victim, his name was Yuan Wenmei, twelve years old. He lived in a village about three miles away from Wujiang, Suzhou (the place name is unknown). His parents were both alive, his father's name was Zhong Sheng, and his grandfather's name was Youqing, who was already seventy-two years old. His brother's nickname was Heshang. The ancestral fields were about thirty mu. Ten days ago, at dusk, more than ten local bandits, each holding a pistol, kidnapped him (the kidnapped victim himself), his grandfather, and his cousin Wensong (twelve years old), the only son of his uncle, to a small steamer, which sailed directly to Shanghai. Upon arriving in Shanghai, the three of them were hidden separately. He was hidden in the bungalow, guarded by three men and one woman in shifts, and suffered abuse. Tonight (i.e., last night), all four bandits were extremely tired and went to sleep. He waited until they were all asleep before lightly opening the door and escaping. On the way, he was fortunate enough to meet a Chinese police officer who rescued him. However, he did not know where his grandfather and cousin were being hidden by the bandits. The chief of detectives, after hearing the confession, ordered the two bandits to be detained separately and issued an order to all detectives to strictly arrest the fugitive bandits and rescue the other two kidnapped victims.

Ren Kang Pawnshop on Zhabei Xinmin Road

Suffers Fire 131

The entire three-section house was almost completely burned down.

Huge losses, fortunately no one was injured.

The Ren Kang Pawnshop at No. 1073, Zhabei Xinmin Road, suddenly caught fire at around 8:00 p.m. yesterday. The entire three-section, twenty-two-room house was completely burned down, causing huge losses. After the fire broke out, the fire brigades of Zhabei immediately drove to the scene and tried their best to put out the fire. However, because the area was large and the clothes and other items were easily ignited, it was not extinguished until around 10:00 p.m. It took about two hours in total. Fortunately, the neighboring houses were not affected and no one was injured.

Ren Kang Pawnshop was founded in the late Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty and has been in business for more than twenty years. The shareholders are Wang, Li, Hu, and others, with a total investment of 50,000 yuan. The current manager, Qian Meisheng, has been in office for many years, and is also the manager of Bao Kang Pawnshop on Gonghe Xin Road, as they are associated stores. Ren Kang house has three sections, the first and second sections have three rooms each and three floors, the last section has two rooms and two floors, for a total of twenty-two rooms. The first section downstairs is the shop, and the upstairs is the clothes room. The second section downstairs is the jewelry room and the money room, and the two floors upstairs are also clothes rooms. The last section is the kitchen and the staff dormitory. There are about twenty-two staff members, from the manager to the package handlers, ticket writers, and students. The business is usually very prosperous, and the credit is also good. It is a giant of the pawnshop industry in Zhabei. Usually, it closes at around 7:30 p.m. If there are many customers, the closing time is extended. At around 8:00 p.m. last night, about forty minutes after closing, a thick smoke suddenly filled the third floor of the front section, followed by flames that went straight to the rear section of the house. In an instant, the flames spewed out from all directions and spread up and down, out of control. All the partners, in addition to sounding the alarm and rescuing, were all pale with fear. After hearing the news, the fire brigades of all sections drove to the scene to put out the fire, but because the house was tall and there were many rooms, the water pressure could not reach effectively. The flames, like snakes, were竄ing between the doors and windows, and in an instant, like rotten wood, the buildings collapsed and all the pledged items were burned to ashes. The exact amount of the loss could not be known for a while. The Public Security Bureau of the Fourth District sent more than 20 police officers to the scene to suppress and detain a ticket clerk named Tan Zhonglin. The manager was out when the fire broke out and had not returned. The house was insured. The cause of the fire is unknown. However, recently, there have been workers working on the upper floor to repair the house, and all of them had left when the fire broke out. The house is the property of Yuanye Company and has been built for many years. Famous jockey.

Determined to Divorce 132

Milna's Magic is Truly Immense

Hu Huilin Does Not Miss the Old Feelings at All

Ms. Fang Has Filed a Counterclaim

The Matter of Reconciliation is Almost Hopeless

Famous jockey Hu Huilin married Ms. Fang Wenxian, the younger sister of Yongshang Fang Jiaobai, sixteen years ago, and they have several children. Since the magician Lande Shan came to Shanghai to perform, Hu and Lande's eldest daughter, Milna, fell in love. Later, Milna went to Tianjin and then abroad with her father, and Hu followed closely behind. Recently, he sent a letter from abroad asking lawyer Wei in Shanghai to file a lawsuit with the Special District Court to allow him to divorce Fang Wenxian. After one summons, the two parties were ordered to reconcile outside of court, as reported in the previous newspaper. Although the mediation was conducted by the lawyers of both parties, it was not very effective. Ms. Fang also ordered her lawyer to file a counterclaim against Hu Huilin, demanding that Hu allocate assets worth 60,000 yuan to provide for her alimony and her children's education expenses. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang Yi opened the court to continue the trial. First, Fang Wenxian's lawyer stated the reasons for the counterclaim, saying that the two had been married for sixteen years and had seven children. The reason Hu filed for divorce this time was entirely because he was infatuated with Milna. It was found that Milna was the daughter of the performer Lande Shan. Lande brought her to Shanghai in the winter of the sixteenth year to perform, and Hu began to fall in love with her. Later, Milna went to Tianjin and then abroad, and Hu also followed. At first, he still provided for the family, but after January of this year, he abandoned his wife and children and asked for a divorce in a letter. His wording was firm, saying that if Ms. Fang did not agree, he would file a criminal lawsuit and never return, which was close to blackmail. The lawyer then presented a photo of Milna and a foreign diary of Hu Huilin as evidence, stating that the photo was given to Hu Huilin by Milna and was titled "Given to My Lover" and expressed the hope that their marriage could be resolved satisfactorily. The lawyer also submitted two letters, one from Hu to Fang before he filed for divorce, expressing three points in the letter: (1) He would not hide any money if he had it (2) He would never take a concubine (3) He would never have two hearts, otherwise he would be a beast. It can be seen that the two were previously harmonious. One was a letter from Hu's sister to Ms. Fang after Hu changed his mind, blaming her brother for changing his mind so quickly, saying that "a man's heart is really unpredictable." However, since Fang's alimony was cut off, she has been living on borrowed money for several months. Now, in addition to not wanting a divorce and demanding an allocation of 60,000 yuan of property, she also asks to have Hu's Baidehua firm and shares in the China Jockey Club seized. Next, Hu Huilin's lawyer stated that the relationship between the two parties has now become irreparable, and the reason for this situation is that Fang Wenxian has made it so. Fang is extravagant and, when money is scarce, she sells Hu's awards. When Hu went abroad to do business in the autumn of last year, he left 2,000 yuan in cash at home. This year, he transferred another 3,500 yuan from Baide. Now she still claims to be living on borrowed money. Spending 5,500 yuan in a few months and still borrowing money is clear proof of extravagance. The most painful thing for Hu is the matter of hiring someone to have an abortion. It is a pity that the person has not been invited to court to prove it. As for whether the photo was titled by Milna, it has not been proven. If Hu has assets, giving 60,000 is not impossible, but Baide is not owned by Hu, and the number of shareholders in the China Jockey Club is only 8,000 and has already been mortgaged. He requested permission to divorce and rejected the counterclaim. Fang's lawyer then took out various awards won by Hu from the trunk, such as gold medals, silver shields, and silver tripods, to prove that they had not been sold. Finally, Prosecutor Xu expressed his opinion, saying that the best solution to this case is reconciliation. If one party insists on divorce, then the other party should be given more compensation for the loss. Judge Yang then announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentence to be announced on the morning of the 27th of this month. He also ordered the two parties to reconcile during this period.

Midwife Deceived 133

Please Perform an Abortion in the Hope of Generous Thanks

Use Ingenious Tactics to Deceive and Take Away Clothing

In recent times, the situation is not peaceful, the world is deteriorating, petty thefts are rampant, and the tricks of deception are becoming more and more refined, making people unpredictable. Recently, it was heard that a new kind of rice seedling technique was discovered in Wusong, so that the victims willingly endured the pain without declaring it. Not only did they not dare to report to the official authorities to arrest them, but even when relatives and friends went to inquire, they were unwilling to tell the truth. They allowed the rogues to wander outside the law. Their plan was truly unsurpassed.

A woman surnamed Yang in the western countryside of Songjiang, over forty years old, whose husband, Jin, had passed away many years ago, leaving behind fields and houses, so that the whole family was able to live in warmth and satiety. Because Yang's mother used to work as a midwife, Yang also knew a little about midwifery surgery. The other day, a person who spoke with a Hakka accent suddenly came to Yang's house and invited her to go to a certain mansion in Shanghai to perform a private abortion. Yang, in the hope of generous thanks, did not scrutinize the matter and rashly agreed. The person, seeing that Yang had agreed, immediately used deceptive tactics, saying that robberies were quite common on the road to Shanghai, so you should take off your gold ring, gold bracelets, silk clothes, etc. and hide them at home to avoid theft. Hearing this, Yang believed it to be golden words and was extremely sincere, so she took off her silk clothes and gold jewelry and went with the person. They boarded the train, and when they arrived at Zhang Huabang Station, the person ordered Yang to get off the train, saying that they had come with a friend, so they should find the friend and return together. You wait here. Yang did not yet know that this was a trick. The person went straight to Yang's house and told Yang's daughter (seventeen years old), "Your mother listened to my words at the time and took off her clothes and jewelry. Now she thinks that Shanghai values clothes and not people, and is afraid of being looked down upon, so she specially ordered me to come and take the clothes and jewelry. If you don't believe me, you can bring the things and go with me to give them to your mother in person." Hearing this, the girl packed the gold jewelry and silk clothes (worth about a hundred yuan) that her mother had taken off into a small package and went with the person. Unexpectedly, the person led the girl to the flag station in Wusong Town and pretended to look for her mother. Before long, the person saw a train arriving and immediately said to the girl, "Your mother is on the train, bring the things here." As he spoke, he forcibly took the package of clothes. The girl was about to board the train, but the train had already started, so she had to return home. After the mother and daughter met, they realized that they had been deceived and could only regret it endlessly. Wusong Hotel.

Teenager Attempts Suicide by Hanging, Saved 134

Unable to Find Work, Wife and Children Flee, Forced to Take This Step

A traveler came to Fuchang Hotel on Songxin Road, Wusong, the previous night and opened room number five. The name written on the circulation book was Xu Ming. That night, the guest closed the door and went to bed. However, by 11:30 a.m. yesterday, he had not gotten up. The tea room was quite surprised and called out from the door, but there was no sound at all. Later, the tea room vaguely saw the guest hanging from the beam from the crack in the door and was greatly alarmed. He immediately reported to the hotel owner, Cai Wenzhi, and reported to the Seventh District Public Security Bureau. At the same time, he tried to break open the door. Fortunately, the guest had not been suicide for long and was still breathing weakly. The tea room untied him and rescued him. After a long time, he recovered. Three suicide notes were found in the drawer of the small table, one to his father, one to his cousin Xu Jiejie (who is currently the Dean of Academics at the Wusong Merchant Marine School), and one to the Fuchang Hotel. The police then took him to the Seventh District Public Security Bureau. After Xu, a staff member, interrogated him, he confessed that his name was Xu Qiutian, 28 years old, from Shaoxing. He used to work in Hangzhou and is now unemployed. He came to Shanghai but could not find work. His clothes were pawned and his wife and children fled home. He had no travel expenses. He went to Wusong the other day but did not meet his cousin Xu Jiejie. Life was so tragic that he had no choice but to take this step. There was no other reason. After hearing the confession, Xu comforted him and then sent the Fuchang owner Cai Wenru to buy him four yuan and sent him to the Shanghai-Hangzhou train to return to his hometown in Shaoxing under police escort from the Seventh District. The letter from Xu Qiutian to his parents is now copied as follows:

To My Dear Parents:

Since I have been unemployed in Hangzhou, I have been to various places to find work but have not found a job. I have been staying at Zhonglin Brother's place for a long time. Land is expensive in Shanghai and I cannot stay for long. I have run out of money. I have tried to find work at my third brother's place in Wusong several times. It was not until the 11th that he replied to me in a letter, saying that I should find another way. I don't even know where my wife and children have gone. Life has been so difficult. After thinking about it again and again, I only have one way to die and end this floating life. I hope you both take care of your health and don't worry about me. If my wife and children return home, tell them to remarry and not to keep an empty room for me. My body can be thrown into the Wusong Yi grave. There is no need to transport it back to my hometown to avoid being talked about by others. With this, I respectfully wish you good health.

Your son, Xu Qiutian, wrote this in desperation.

Public Works Committee Meeting of the Shanghai Municipal Council 137

June 3rd, 4:30 PM, the Shanghai Municipal Council held a Public Works Committee meeting. Present: Mr. Bair, Mr. Reis Lien, Mr. Hutch, Mr. Yuan Ludeng, Director of Public Works, Director of Accounting, Deputy General Manager, etc. Mr. Bair chaired the meeting. The minutes of the discussed cases are as follows: (1) Approved the minutes of the previous meeting. (2) Case of increased transportation costs for the Pingqiao stone quarry. The contractor of the Pingqiao stone quarry has requested the Council to revise the contract terms due to the increase in transportation costs. The Director of Public Works reported that the waterway through which the stone-carrying vessels pass is currently blocked due to dredging and will be closed for about eight months. During this period, all vessels must detour, which was not taken into account in the contract. Since the merchant has submitted a request, a subsidy of 5,000 taels should be given. After discussion, the case was approved by all members. (3) Case of collecting surcharges for land acquisition. Mr. Brooke, Chairman of the Land Commission for this year, wrote to the Council inquiring how the method of land purchase and pricing should be regulated, as disputes often arise on the matter at the meetings. The Deputy General Manager is in charge of the case files and debates on this issue. The main point of the debate is whether a subsidy of one-tenth of the original price should be given for compulsory land acquisition for road construction. Mr. Brooke's opinion is that since Shanghai is an international public concession, the Land Commission cannot be bound by the laws of any country, and the methods formulated by the commissioners should be based on equality. The Deputy General Manager stated that according to the case files, the method of land acquisition for road construction has been implemented since the Land Regulations of 1919, which overturned the one-tenth of a percent fee method in the Land Regulations of 1845, because this subsidy method does not exist in European and American countries. Last year, the purchase of land on North Sichuan Road from the Ye Guang Company was not given a subsidy, but the company is still demanding it. Although Mr. Brooke proposed that the Land Commission should not be controlled by the laws of any country, his proposal to adopt equality is not supported, because the Council's method of land purchase and pricing should be handled according to the Land Boundary Regulations. Therefore, the Land Commission should also base its valuation of land on the Land Boundary Regulations. The method of land purchase and pricing has always been stipulated in the Land Boundary Regulations, but the subsidy of 11% has not been noted in the regulations, so the Council has no right to pay it. Even if a subsidy is sometimes given, it is only considered an extra compensation and cannot be considered a formal regulation. Although Section B of Article 6 of the Regulations stipulates a percentage of compulsory purchase fees for land acquisition for railway construction, Section A of Article 6 does not specify this when acquiring land for public use. However, the owners often believe that this land subsidy should still be issued, but they do not know that the Council's method of pricing is based on the Land Boundary Regulations. Therefore, the Committee replied to Mr. Brooke stating that the Land Commission's method of determining land prices is based on the Land Boundary Regulations. (4) Case of widening North Suzhou Road and National Day Road. According to the width of National Day Road widened in the Chinese area, the Director of Public Works intends to purchase land from Land Registry Book No. 1, with an area of 3.16 acres and a price of 18,940 taels (including engineers' fees). Although this land is not within the designated route, the Director of Public Works is aware that the owner is very willing to change the design and sell this land so that the rest of the property can be developed. All the above discussed items have been approved. The meeting adjourned at 5:40 PM.

Clearing of Floating Coffins in the North and South City 138

The Sanitary Bureau has previously sent personnel to investigate no less than several thousand cases of floating coffins in the city. With the summer approaching, they pose a major obstacle to sanitation. It is now known that Sanitary Bureau Chief Hu Hongji, together with the Public Security Bureau, has already cleared all floating coffins with or without owners within the North and South City limits. The original report submitted to the city government for filing is recorded as follows: A report is hereby submitted for the matter of reporting the case of banning floating coffins in the city. Previously, the bureau and other authorities jointly issued a proclamation ordering the coffin owners to move the coffins themselves. All ownerless coffins were to be buried by charitable organizations. A meeting was also convened with various charitable organizations to discuss and decide to start with the North and South City. Later, the Pushan Villa reported that the burial situation in the South City was slightly different from the reports of various districts. The bureau then urged them to continue to be responsible for handling the matter, and to clear the floating coffins in the North and South City as soon as possible. Order No. 4991 of the Superior Government was approved for filing. Now, according to the Pushan Villa's letter, although there are thousands of floating coffins in the South City, the coffins with owners have all been moved by themselves. All 195 ownerless coffins previously reported to have been buried have been verified by the district land guards and buried in accordance with the resolution. They have now been cleared. The above-mentioned sections are true. As for the floating coffins in other districts, they should be buried in order as soon as possible to supplement the original case. In addition to the bureau and other authorities convening another meeting of the municipal commissioners of various districts and various charitable organizations to discuss methods and actively proceed, a written report is hereby submitted for consideration and filing.

The Two Guarantors Are Relieved of a Heavy Burden 144

The 630,000 major fraud case, which was originally scheduled to be sentenced on the 29th of last month after the debate was concluded, was not sentenced on the due date because He Qiqing, who was released on bail, had disappeared without a trace and a warrant was issued for his arrest. The two copper-making households who had guaranteed He were responsible for the guarantee and searched everywhere. At first, they went to He's house in Zhabei, but it had already been moved. According to Cao, Yang Shulin fled on the sixteenth day of the first lunar month. The next day, the clerk of his business received a letter and learned about it. Then, the tea servant of the Tongzhou Steamboat sent Yang's letter, saying that he was injured after being kidnapped and was being treated at the Weihaiwei Hospital. It was not until the tea servant of the Dongya Travel Report received a letter from Yang in Tianjin that he learned that the previous claims of being kidnapped were all lies. He then sent someone to Tianjin to persuade him to come to Shanghai and open an Anle Palace hotel to settle the accounts. However, he immediately thought of escaping and hired a car with his concubine Chen Huanxi to escape. He first pointed out his partner He Shiqing, and He confessed that Yang was hiding in the Guangdong Hotel on North Sichuan Road, so he went to arrest him. He's suffering was entirely deceived by Xie Kai, because Xie was his clerk and Yang's manager, and he always boasted that Yang's business was prosperous, which led to his being deceived. Then, Chen, a member of the Zhabei Fire Brigade, stated that the association had deposited a total of more than 8,000 yuan in the Wenji Hexing companies, involving dozens of people. Judge Sun then questioned Yang about the use of the money. Yang still claimed that it was for interest payments and business failures. He Qiqing, who was questioned, evaded the issue and hired a lawyer to request that he be allowed to be released on bail. However, the lawyer of the police station and the lawyers of the creditors all expressed their opposition. Judge Sun ordered the two defendants to be taken into custody pending sentencing on the morning of the 17th of this month.

The Key Criminal in the Kidnapping Case Has Been Arrested 145

Shen Yinbin Was Sent to Minhang 146

Yan Arong, the son of Yan Duanchen, a merchant in Nanhui, Fengxian, and Tanzhi Bridge South in Pudong, is 28 years old. The kidnapping case that occurred in early March of this year was reported to the governments of Nanhui and Fengxian counties and the Public Security Bureau for strict investigation. After many days, the case has not been solved. It is now known that Shen Yinbin, the key criminal in this case, was hiding in Shanghai and was arrested by Zhang Quanzhou, a detective from the First District of the Jiangsu Water Police stationed in Minhang, at 7:00 AM on the 8th in Pudong and sent to the First District of Minhang for questioning.

Private Minting of Counterfeit Coins Discovered 147

Yang Ning'an, a native of Ningbo, was arrested on North Henan Road and found with 25 counterfeit Shuangjiao coins on his person. He was taken to the Huishi Police Station for investigation. According to Yang, he bought them from Zhu Zhisheng, a native of Suzhou, for 15 counterfeit Shuangjiao coins per yuan. The time of the transaction was every day at 8:00 or 9:00 AM, and the location was on the Suzhou River on North Chengdu Road. Chinese and Western detectives went to the address on the previous morning and arrested Zhu. They found more than 100 Shuangjiao coins on his person. According to Zhu, the private minting facility was located at No. 5 Rangde Lane, Baoshan Road, Zhabei. Detectives from the police station went to the facility and found 37 yuan of lead-containing silver dollars, 429 lead-containing Shuangjiao coins, two sets of molds for making fake silver dollars, nine sets of molds for fake Shuangjiao coins, two dry batteries, and white powder, as well as Chen Liansheng and Ye Mujin. They were temporarily detained at the police station. Yesterday morning, Zhu Zhisheng was sent to the Special District Local Court. Judge Sun questioned the police station lawyer and requested to prepare a document to take away the physical evidence and witnesses and postpone the trial. Zhu confessed that he had been idle for a long time, and Chen and Ye asked him to send hundreds of lead coins to the Xinzha Bridge every morning and give them to a man named Yang, who would pay him five yuan. He received a wage of six jiao per day. Judge Sun ordered Zhu to be detained and rescheduled the trial.

One Couple Escaped, Two 148

Xu Shi Caught Adultery, But Caught Nothing 149

Bao Shi Visited a Friend and Was Arrested Xu Shi (44 years old), a native of Chongming, had no children and owned a small property. She was about to adopt her nephew Yunlong as her son. Yunlong was already in his teens and his mother had arranged for him to marry Wang Xiuzhen (19 years old), a fellow villager. Xiuzhen had bright eyes and white teeth and was very beautiful, and she had received a higher education. After marrying into the family, she saw that her husband was blind in one eye and had rough black skin, like a country bumpkin, and she had no affection for him. Xiuzhen was unhappy and felt sorry for herself for marrying the wrong person. A neighbor, Lu Fu, was young and handsome and loved to dress up. Seeing Xiuzhen's beauty and marrying a fool, he was unhappy and took the opportunity to seduce Xiuzhen with sweet words. Lu was a talented and gentle man, and the two fell in love. However, Xiuzhen's husband and aunt were very strict in their surveillance. Although they secretly met, they could not satisfy their desires, so they decided to elope. They agreed to secretly flee to Shanghai some time ago. Xu Shi learned that her daughter-in-law was abducted by Lu Fu, so she followed her to Shanghai and stayed at her relative's house to search for her. The day before yesterday, she met a fellow villager who told her the location of Xiuzhen's residence. She went to the Guang'an Hotel on North Zhejiang Road and asked about room 35, where Lu and Xiuzhen were staying together. Lu and his friend Bao Shi (a native of Wuxi) and Xiuzhen were in the room talking. After hearing Xu Shi's voice, Lu realized that things were not going well and immediately escaped through the back door without a trace. Xiuzhen waited for her aunt to enter the room and then pretended to be diligent and went out to pour tea, also taking the opportunity to escape. Only Lu's friend Bao Shi and Xu Shi were left in the room. Later, because Xiuzhen did not return, she knew she had escaped and called the police to take Bao to the First Section of the Fourth District. After questioning by Chief Yao, Bao Shi confessed that he was 22 years old and was a friend of Lu and did not know about the abduction of Xiuzhen. The chief of the section, believing that the case involved adultery and abduction, prepared a document yesterday and sent it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for verification.

A Father Doesn't Want His Unfaithful Daughter 150

Wang Nenghai, a native of Wusong and a former steward, whose residence is located at No. 2, White Sai Zhong Road, French Concession, has a second daughter, Wang Shuzhen, who is not yet married at the age of 20. This spring, she went to her sister's husband, Chen Guitang, to visit her sister, and had a relationship with her brother-in-law, Chen Guitang. She stayed for a long time and did not return. Her father, Wang Nenghai, learned about this and reported it to the police station, ordering the detectives to arrest Chen and Shuzhen and bring them to the French Public Hall. They were ordered to verify the situation, which has been reported in the previous report. Yesterday, they were again summoned for questioning. The plaintiff claimed that his daughter was so indecent that he did not want to take her back and asked to allow his younger brother to take her away. The Chinese and Western officials sentenced Chen Guitang to three months of imprisonment with a three-year suspension. Wang Shuzhen was taken back by her aunt and disciplined. The father hopes that his daughter will correct her mistakes.

A Father Came Back After Ten Years Abroad, and the Father and Son Questioned Each Other Without Understanding 151

Wu Xinglong, a 56-year-old native of Zhenjiang residing on Haixing Road in Pudong, is a barber. His son, Changgen, is 30 years old and works with his father. He left home ten years ago and did not return until February of this year. Then, he and his wife moved to the vicinity of Tuditang. His wife, Zhang, works in the British-American Tobacco Factory. Recently, Wu and Changgen often quarreled because Changgen was addicted to gambling and had not changed his ways. They fought and were taken to the Third District Police Station together, and Zhang also arrived at the same time. After questioning by the district chief, Xinglong confessed that his son Changsheng was addicted to gambling and had been warned repeatedly but did not change his ways. He left home ten years ago without saying goodbye and still had not changed his ways when he returned. His gambling had impoverished the family and requested that he be ordered to change his ways. According to Changsheng, Xinglong is not his biological father. Soon after he married, he actually committed the act of "digging ashes," having an affair with his wife Zhang. Therefore, he was extremely angry and left home ten years ago to do business and did not want to witness this scandal at home. This year, when he returned home, he saw that the two were still cohabiting, so he moved his wife to another place to sever their relationship. Now, Xinglong, seeing that he had not succeeded, accused him of interfering with gambling and instead sought trouble with him. At that time, Xinglong continued to say that Changsheng was indeed not his biological son, but he adopted him and raised him when he was eight years old. His wife Zhang was also raised in his home when she was seven years old. At that time, he treated the two as children. Later, when they grew up, he made the decision to marry them and turn them into his children and grandchildren, hoping that he would have someone to rely on when he was old. How dare he imitate the act of "digging ashes" and ruin his reputation? Zhang confessed that her husband Changgen was indeed too addicted to gambling, which caused great turmoil in the family. Her clothes were also pawned by him. If he could immediately change his ways, the family could still be harmonious as before. She also strongly denied the claim of having an affair with her father-in-law. The district chief intended to mediate and sentenced Changsheng to five days of detention to show his repentance and appease Xinglong's anger. Unexpectedly, Changgen roared loudly, claiming that he was not satisfied with the detention and would rather go to court to clarify what was good and what was evil. The district chief, seeing that the two sides could not resolve the issue peacefully, allowed both parties, along with Zhang, to be sent to the Local Court for questioning.

A Neighbor Woman's Room Was Broken into Late at Night 152

Zhou Younian Was Brazen and Lewd 153

Ge Zhang, a 25-year-old woman from Taixing who lives in a shed in the Huifeng Oil Factory in West Shanghai, works in a cotton mill. Her husband, Ge, often travels with the ship because he works on the ship and only occasionally returns home. The woman is usually very frugal. Recently, Zhou Younian, a neighbor, saw that the woman was living alone at home and wanted to take advantage of her, but had no opportunity. He would occasionally make jokes, but the woman ignored him. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at about 9:00 PM, Zhou's animal instincts erupted. He entered her room while she was about to sleep and pressed her on the bed and raped her. Seeing that she was weak and could not resist, the woman shouted loudly. Zhou was afraid and fled. As soon as he went out, he was grabbed by the woman, who used all her strength, and called the police, who arrested him and brought him to the First Section of the Sixth District Police Station. After questioning by Chief Ren, the plaintiff Zhang confessed that she was 25 years old and from Taixing. The defendant Zhou Younian confessed that he was 30 years old and from Taizhou. After obtaining the confessions, Chief Ren, believing that the case involved the rape of a woman, immediately prepared a document and sent it to the court for questioning.

A Car Accident Caused Harm 154

Three Pedestrians Were Injured 155

Shen Gaofu, a native of Yuyao, was driving a car on Datong Road in Zhabei yesterday at about 11:30 AM when the driver accidentally hit three pedestrians, Yin Youke, Xu Guisheng, and Xu Chen. The police took Shen to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau. Shen claimed that he was visiting his friend Yang A'quan, who runs a car business on Datong Road. Seeing a car parked on the side of the road, he thought it was driven by Yang, so he got in and tried to drive it, but accidentally injured someone. He asked for forgiveness. The district chief ordered him to be sent to the Judicial Section for verification. The injured Yin Youke is a native of Yongkang and resides at No. 25 Changan Road. He was injured in his waist, legs, and back. Xu Guisheng, 37 years old, is a native of Changshu and resides at No. 2126 Xiexing Lane, Wenjian Temple Road. He is a vendor and was injured in both feet. His wife, Chen, was injured in her waist and back. All were sent to the hospital for treatment.

A Shoemaker Was Stabbed by a Foe 156

Ji Xingsheng Brought It On Himself 157

Ji Xingsheng, a 26-year-old shoemaker from Changzhou, was drinking tea at Qule Garden on Tangshan Road at around 2:30 PM yesterday when he was stabbed in the right waist by a foe with a sharp blade, causing four wounds. Ji called the police, and the Chinese police from the Huishan Police Station arrested the murderer, Shui Xiangsheng. Those who know the details say that Shui, 39 years old and from Jiangyin, was also a partner in Wu Shunxing's shoe shop last year. This year, he was dismissed and worked in a shoe shop in Xujiahui. His wife is 12 years younger than Shui. She came to Shanghai last week, went straight to Wu Shunxing's to find her husband, and met Ji Xingsheng and Zhou Bingsheng, who told her that her husband had been dismissed and was now working in Xujiahui. However, their words were malicious. Shui's wife wanted to see her husband, so Zhou Bingsheng accompanied her to Xujiahui to find him, but they did not meet him. Then, Zhou borrowed a dollar from a friend and led the woman to the Xihua Hotel on Huaji Road. Whether or not there was any illicit behavior between the two is unknown to outsiders. However, Shui Xiangsheng heard about this and was very angry. Yesterday afternoon, he invited Ji and Zhou to Jule Garden to drink tea and reason with them. When they disagreed, he suddenly used a blade to stab Ji, causing him to be injured. Ji is now being treated at the Tongren Hospital, and it can be said that he brought it on himself.

The Murder Case at the Umami Mother Factory Has Been Prosecuted 158

Chen Ruian and Chen Fengshan, who were arrested for causing a conflict between outsiders and workers at the factory of the Tianyi Umami Mother Food Company at No. 784 Taopeng Road, have been sent to the Special District Local Court for questioning, as reported in this newspaper. After this case occurred, Tong A'qing, the foreman of Tianyi, claimed that Zhang Shoupeng, the property manager of Jiecheng Silver Company, the landlord, had instigated the incident. He went to Zhang's house to argue with him, so Zhang hired a lawyer to sue Tong. Yesterday morning, Judge Ge questioned them and simultaneously questioned the two Chens. According to Tianyi's worker Ma Rongzhang and others, Chen Fengshan was holding an axe during the conflict and Zhang Shoupeng was actually instigating the incident. When questioned, Chen Ruian confessed that he was mistaken for a thug because he was passing by and was struck on the head. Chen Fengshan also denied participating in the attack. Then, Zhang Shoupeng confessed that he was the accounting clerk of Jiecheng's leased property. Tianyi initially only rented eight rooms and now wants to rent several more rooms. So, he tried to force the old tenants to move out and rent to Tianyi, so Tianyi agreed to give him 60 yuan every year and 20 yuan for each festival. He did not know about the fight that day. Tong A'qing, the foreman of Tianyi, gathered a crowd to look for trouble at his house after the incident. Fortunately, he escaped through the back door. Moreover, Tianyi's staff proved that the leaser of Jiecheng was the lawyer Jiang Yiping and Zhang was only a helper and now falsely claims to be the accounting clerk. Liu Baoshan, the detective in charge, stated that there were accusations of police officers crossing boundaries to make arrests and accepting bribes in Zhang Shoupeng's complaint and must charge Peng with false accusations. Judge Ge ordered the two Chens to be remanded in custody and Zhang and Peng each to pay 500 yuan in bail pending further investigation.

Autopsy of the Murder Case of a Worker Who Was Hacked to Death 159

The worker Yu Henian of the Peilin Egg Factory in Yangshupu was hacked to death at the factory gate at 5:05 AM the day before yesterday by Yang Mingde and other workers from the same factory who gathered gangsters. This has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Guo Huaipu, the prosecutor of the Special District Court, arrived at the scene of the autopsy to examine the body. According to the witness Ye Jicai, the deceased went to A'hai's house to gamble and lost more than ten yuan. He was very unhappy and took away the dice used for gambling, which caused a rift with Yang Mingde and others, who were A'hai's companions. He was not present at the scene and could not say whether Yang was the murderer. Moreover, Yu A'long, the father of the deceased, claimed that his son had been brutally killed and demanded justice. Mr. Guo, after obtaining the confession, stated that the deceased Yu Henian had indeed been hacked to death by Yang Mingde and others with an axe before his death. He ordered the police to arrest the murderer and bring him to justice. The body was to be collected by the father of the deceased.

An Elderly Woman from Jiangbei Drowns Out of Panic 160

Yesterday morning at approximately 9:10 AM, near the second bridge in the vicinity of the Rihui Port Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, an elderly woman, appearing to be about fifty years old and of Jiangbei origin, was walking on the bridge. The fourth express train from the South Station to Hangzhou approached, and in a moment of panic, the woman was unable to avoid it, causing her to fall into the river and drown. The station police immediately went to the rescue, recovered the body, and informed the local bailiff to report to the local court for an inquest. They also sought out the deceased's relatives to come to the station to identify the body, prepare a coffin, and arrange for burial.

Robbery at a Cloth Firm 161

The Tongan Factory Cloth Firm, located at No. 2 Tongan Lane, Limalu Road in the South City, is a joint venture of the six major cloth businesses in the South City, specializing in collecting cloth from various factories and distributing it to the member businesses for sale. The business is quite large. Consequently, from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM daily, various factories gather to deliver goods, with quantities exceeding thousands of bolts, and expenditures amounting to thousands of dollars. The accountant position is rotated daily among the member businesses. Yesterday afternoon, at around 3:00 PM, while the firm was busy with business, four robbers suddenly appeared. One was wearing a navy blue serge long gown, and the other three robbers wore white and blue striped short shirts and trousers, and a yellow Zhongshan suit, respectively. They all spoke with a northern accent. After entering the gate, each robber drew a pistol from their chest and drove the more than twenty accountants, partners, and factory friends into a corner, forbidding them from making a sound. One of the robbers wearing a long gown guarded the front door, while one wearing a Zhongshan suit guarded the back door. The remaining two robbers entered the accounting room, opened the drawer containing silver dollars on the accounting table, and took all the $3,298 in banknotes and silver dollars (mostly from the China Industrial Bank), as well as 129 small silver coins. After taking the loot, they calmly left. The two robbers guarding the front and back doors, seeing that their goal had been achieved, also left one after another, closing the door and fleeing without a trace. According to the firm, the two robbers who seized the cash first pulled out the drawer containing the money, and after taking the banknotes and silver dollars, left without touching other places. Their actions suggest that they were quite familiar with the firm's internal affairs.

Report on the Activities of the Tuberculosis Sanatorium 162

The report on the activities of the Tuberculosis Sanatorium at No. 2 Da Xi Road in this city for the last quarter is as follows: 217 initial consultations, 868 follow-up consultations, 221 X-ray examinations, and 112 hospitalizations. Among those hospitalized, 56% recovered and 7% died. The average length of hospitalization was 32 days. Among them, 26 patients with stage III pulmonary tuberculosis underwent artificial pneumothorax surgery to collapse the cavities. Except for those with complications such as laryngeal tuberculosis or intestinal tuberculosis, most turned from danger to safety, with extremely good results. The sanatorium hopes that hospitals in the interior will adopt this method to eradicate the disease. It is reported that relatives of Zhou Yiwen of the Ministry of Railways and Lin Xiang, President of the Supreme Court, have recently undergone surgery at the sanatorium and are about to be discharged.

Wang Wencai Accused of Malfeasance and Embezzlement 163

On March 24th, Huang Zhenrong, a patrolman from the First District Police Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, apprehended a case of smuggling opium at the 16th Pier. Subsequently, the First District Police Station transferred the opium smuggler Qian Degen and three sacks of opium to the local court for prosecution. Later, Huang Zhenrong testified in court that the person he arrested was a car driver, not Qian Degen, who resembled a vagrant. He also claimed that there was a car used to transport the opium and that there were five sacks of opium. He accused his patrol officer Wang Wencai of accepting a large bribe to release the suspect, substituting a vagrant, and embezzling the opium. At the time, Officer Wang was summoned for questioning, stating that Huang Zhenrong harbored resentment for being transferred to the Sixth District and was slandering him. After review by the Public Trial Court, it was determined that the evidence was insufficient for the time being, and if Wang Wencai had indeed engaged in illegal behavior, the prosecutor should investigate. Therefore, the Criminal Court first concluded part of the Qian Degen case without issuing a verdict. However, after the Qian Degen case was concluded, Huang Zhenrong filed a complaint with the prosecutor's office, accusing Wang Wencai of malfeasance and embezzlement. After the court approved the complaint, it ordered Huang Zhenrong to surrender himself for questioning and verification. Yesterday afternoon, after reading the approval, Huang Zhenrong surrendered himself to the prosecutor's office. Prosecutor Yang opened the court for preliminary examination and ordered him to be dismissed pending verification.

Union News 165

The Postal Workers' Union held its 32nd Executive Committee meeting the day before yesterday. Chairman Qi Jiamou (1) presided over the meeting and conducted the proceedings according to etiquette. (2) Matters reported (omitted). (3) Matters discussed: (a) The Standing Committee Secretariat proposed whether it is feasible to print and designate a responsible commissioner to edit the work report of this session. Please make a public decision on the matter. (Resolved) Passed and nominated Zhao Shusheng, Qi Jiamou, and Zhu Xuefan to be responsible for handling the matter. (b) The Standing Committee proposed that the Postal Administration ordered the Shanghai Bureau to conduct a clerical examination, which, according to the current postal bureau transfer method, seems to be superfluous. Moreover, judging from the facts, very few bureau members have registered. It is proposed to suggest that the Postal Administration can directly select and transfer the required clerical staff to Shanghai Bureau from various departments. Is this feasible? Please discuss. (Resolved) Passed and forwarded to the Shanghai Bureau. (c) Standing Committee member Zhang Kechang submitted a report on the review of the salary rate for operating elevators, with attached opinions. Please make a public decision on the matter. (Resolved) Handed over to the Standing Committee to handle together with the case of revising the salary rate for miscellaneous workers. (d) The Secretariat proposed that, in accordance with the decided case, members should be designated to be responsible for compiling and printing the association's membership directory. (Resolved) Passed and handed over to the Organization Department for handling. (e) The Standing Committee proposed to review the process of the temporary subsidy issue for the association's employees and attach opinions. Please make a public decision on the matter. (Resolved) The association's employees should receive a temporary monthly subsidy of two yuan. The starting rice price and effective period should follow the regulations of the Postal Bureau. (f) The carter Guan Tingzuo submitted a request for reinstatement because he was accidentally hit and killed by a French sailor. The French public office has ruled that there is no serious crime, so how should the reinstatement be handled? Please discuss. (Resolved) Negotiate with the authorities. (g) Member Tan Meicun submitted a request for an increase in salary that has not been received on time. Please have the association negotiate with the authorities. (Resolved) Instruct the Secretariat to reply by letter. (h) All messengers submitted a request on how to participate in the postal assistant examination. Please discuss. (Resolved) Nominate Zhu Yinghua and Zhu Xuefan to be responsible for periodically convening meetings of all messengers to report on the progress of negotiations and provide explanations. (i) The Standing Committee proposed to amend the public gratuity regulations. Please discuss. (Remainder omitted.) (4) Temporary motions: (a) Messengers and errand boys with more than fifteen years of service who have passed a simplified examination to become postal assistants have been ordered by the Postal Administration to be limited to one time by the Shanghai Bureau, which still does not meet the association's requirements. The case should be continued to be negotiated. (Resolved) Passed and negotiated with the authorities. (b) The Postal Administration ordered the Shanghai Bureau that messengers who are disabled due to official duties and have served for more than fifteen years are only allowed to be in-house messengers, and the quota is limited to ten people, which is still inconsistent with the association's requirements. The case should be continued to be negotiated. (Resolved) Passed and negotiated with the authorities. (c) (The West District of this Bureau always delegates ordinary internal and surgical diseases to hospitals for treatment, and the dispensary is not fully equipped. It is suggested that the authorities strengthen the rectification. (Resolved) Passed. (d) The dead letter office sometimes finds various medicines that cannot be delivered. It is suggested that the Bureau's medical examination office selects them for waste utilization. (Resolved) Suggest to the authorities. (e) Read and amend the meeting minutes. Adjourned.

Weather Report 166

The forecast from the Xujiahui Observatory at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that there are southeast seasonal winds over the East China Sea and the Yellow Sea, with southerly winds to the north, and gentle, undirected winds and fog along the southern coast. The local weather is cloudy with showers. Also, in the four hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 83.1 degrees and the lowest was 68.7 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 83.7 degrees and the lowest was 70.7 degrees. Letter received.

Regarding the news item published in the museum on the 3rd of this month concerning the presentation of the color industry contract, lawyer Mu Ansu wrote yesterday, stating that, according to the party involved, Lihe Foreign Firm, Judge Yang of the Civil Court of the local court, at the request of lawyer Ma Shangjie, instructed the Color Association to come forward to mediate, which is inconsistent with the facts. The case should be negotiated by Ma Shangjie and Lihe Foreign Firm, and the Color Association has no right to intervene. Moreover, the Color Association should not arbitrarily comment on cases that have not been decided by the court. Lihe Foreign Firm said so. It is specially translated and recorded to correct it. The women's work in Huangyan, Zhejiang has always been dominated by weaving white cloth, straw mats, towels, and cotton socks, followed by drawing lamp cores and pasting light fans. However, the income from the above items is meager. Last year, because the wage for weaving foreign straw hats was higher, those who were quick could earn 30 cents a day. Therefore, they heard the news and rushed to abandon their old jobs and learn to weave foreign straw hats. It is said that the daily average export volume from Haimen can reach 10,000 yuan. The county's rice was eaten by insects last year, followed by the great wind and water of the seventh month of the lunar calendar, and the upper and lower seasons were almost barren. All the general farm women rely on the income from this work to fill their stomachs, otherwise, relying solely on the government's funds and local rich people's efforts to open water wheels will be of no avail, and they will inevitably die in the gullies.
